PREFACE
   This code of the City of Genesee, as supplemented, contains ordinances up to
and including resolution 2023-4, passed October 17, 2023. Ordinances of the
City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
                     American Legal Publishing
                     Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not affect the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NO. 269
AN ORDINANCE PROVIDING FOR THE REVISION, CODIFICATION AND COMPILATION OF THE
GENERAL ORDINANCES OF THE CITY OF GENESEE.
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF GENESEE, IDAHO:
   Section 1. That all ordinances of a general nature now in force in the City
of Genesee, Idaho, as revised, codified and compiled and hereinafter set forth,
be, and they are hereby adopted, passed, published and declared to be the
compiled ordinances of the City of Genesee, pursuant to Chapter 9, Title 50 of
the Idaho Code, as amended, empowering any city of the first or second class,
or any village, to revise, codify and compile its ordinances.
   Section 2. That this ordinance and all said ordinances of a general nature
compiled and codified as above stated, shall be in full force and effect upon
the passage, approval, and publication of this ordinance in one issue of The
Gazette News, a newspaper of general circulation, published in the City of
Kendrick, Idaho, Latah County, and the official newspaper thereof.
   Adopted February 7, 1983.

CHAPTER 1
GENESEE CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Construction Of Words
1-1-5: Definitions
1-1-6: Liability Of Employers And Agents
1-1-1: TITLE:
This compilation and codification of the general ordinances of the city of
Genesee is hereby declared to be and shall hereafter constitute the official
city code of the city of Genesee. Any reference made to the number of any
section contained herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the
same under its appropriate title heading, its chapter heading, and its section
heading, and to the general penalty clause relating thereto, as well as to the
section itself, when reference is made to this code by title in any legal
documents. (1963 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in all administrative tribunals of this
state as the ordinances of a general and permanent effect of the city. (1963
Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending this code shall set forth the title, chapter and section
number of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall constitute a
sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to the
amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to Sterling
Codifiers, Inc., and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for
insertion in its proper place in each copy of this code. Each such replacement
page shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in each copy of this
code within thirty (30) days from the date of its final passage. (1963 Code)
1-1-4: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
Whenever any word in any section of this code importing the plural number is
used, in describing or referring to any matters, parties, or persons, any
single matter, party or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used. When any subject matter, party or
person is referred to in this code by words importing the singular number only,
or the masculine gender, several matters, parties, or persons and females as
well as males and bodies corporate shall be deemed to be included. Provided,
that these rules of construction shall not be applied to any section of this
code which contains any express provision excluding such construction or where
the subject matter or content may be repugnant thereto. (1963 Code)
1-1-5: DEFINITIONS:
   KNOWINGLY: Imports only a knowledge that the facts exist which brings the
act or omission within the provisions of this code. It does not require any
knowledge of the unlawfulness of such act or omission.
   NEGLECT, NEGLIGENCE, NEGLIGENT, AND NEGLIGENTLY: Imports a want of such
attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission as a
prudent man ordinarily bestows in acting in his own concern.
   OFFICER: Shall include officers and boards in charge of departments and
members of such boards. The word "city", "clerk", "treasurer", or other such
title shall mean city clerk, city treasurer, or other city officer as the use
may be applicable.
   OWNER: Applied to a building or land shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
   PERSON: Shall be deemed to include any "person, firm, association, or
corporation" or any organization of any kind.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right or
interest therein.
   STREETS: Includes alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
   TENANT OR OCCUPANT: Applied to a building or land shall include any person
who occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or
with others.
   WILFULLY: When applied to the intent with which an act is done or omitted,
implies simply a purpose or willingness to commit the act or make the omission
referred to. It does not require any intent to violate law, or to injure
another, or to acquire an advantage.
   WRITTEN AND IN WRITING: May include printing.
Words prohibiting anything being done, except in accordance with a license or
permit or authority from a board or officer, shall be construed as giving such
board or officer power to license or permit or authorize such thing to be done.
(1963 Code)
1-1-6: LIABILITY OF EMPLOYERS AND AGENTS:
When the provisions of any section of this official code prohibits the
commission of an act, not only the person actually doing the prohibited act or
omitting the directed act, but also the employer and all other persons
concerned with or in aiding or abetting the said person shall be deemed guilty
of the offense described and liable to the penalty set forth. (1963 Code; amd.
1982 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Pending Suits
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the city passed prior to the passage of this code are
hereby repealed, except such as are referred to herein as being still in force
or are by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the
saving clauses herein contained) from which are excluded the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances, appropriation
ordinances, ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations, franchise
ordinances, and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations, contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants, salary ordinances, ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places,
improvement ordinances, bond ordinances, ordinances relating to elections,
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
city and all special ordinances. (1963 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroads or railroad crossings with streets and other
public ways, or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public
utilities shall be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this code or by virtue
of the preceding section, excepting as this code may contain provision for such
matters, in which case this code shall be considered as amending such ordinance
or ordinances in respect of such provisions only. (1963 Code)
1-2-3: PENDING SUITS:
No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former ordinance,
whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any offense
committed against such former ordinance or as town act done, any penalty,
forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrue or claim arising
under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any such offense
or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so
incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new ordinance takes
effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform to the
ordinances in force at the time of such proceedings, so far as practicable. If
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any provision of a new
ordinance, such provision may be, by the consent of the party affected, applied
to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes effect.
This section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or
implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions
upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
Nothing contained in this or the preceding sections shall be construed as
abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general ordinance of
the city herein repealed; or as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering
any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person,
firm, or corporation, or as waiving any right of the city under any ordinance
or provision thereof in force at the time of adoption of this code. (1963 Code)
CHAPTER 3
CLAIMS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Claims Filed With City Clerk
1-3-2: Claims For Damages
1-3-1: CLAIMS FILED WITH CITY CLERK:
All claims against the city must be filed with the city clerk, in writing, and
by him presented to the council for their auditing, with a full account of the
item, verified by the oath of the claimant, or his agent, that the same is
correct, reasonable and just and that it nor any part thereof has not been
paid, and no claims or demands shall be audited or allowed unless presented and
verified as provided for in this section. (1963 Code)
1-3-2: CLAIMS FOR DAMAGES:
All claims for damages against the city must be filed with the clerk, within
six (6) months after the time when such claim for damages shall have accrued,
specifying, the time, place, character and cause of said damages. No action
shall be maintained against the city for any claim for damages until the same
has been presented to the council, and until sixty (60) days have elapsed after
such presentation. The allowance of any or all damage claims against such city
shall be by ordinance and not otherwise. (1963 Code)
CHAPTER 4
CORPORATE SEAL
SECTION:
1-4-1: Corporate Seal; Design
1-4-2: Adoption Of Seal
1-4-3: City Clerk Custodian Of Seal
1-4-1: CORPORATE SEAL; DESIGN:
The corporate seal of the city of Genesee, Idaho, shall be circular in form
with inner and outer circles of a rope design. The outer circle shall be one
and seven-eighths inches (17/8") in diameter and the inner circle shall be one
and three-sixteenths inches (13/16") in diameter. It shall bear upon the upper
portion of space between the two (2) circles the words "City of Genesee", and
upon the lower portion of the space between the two (2) circles the words
"Latah Co. Idaho", and upon the space within the inner circle shall be the
illustration of grain and harvest tools.
A facsimile of the above described seal is shown below:
[IMAGE]
(1963 Code)
1-4-2: ADOPTION OF SEAL:
The seal described in section
 1-4-1 of this chapter is hereby adopted as the corporate seal of the city of
Genesee, Latah County, Idaho. (1963 Code)
1-4-3: CITY CLERK CUSTODIAN OF SEAL:
The clerk of the city shall be the custodian of the corporate seal and shall
affix said seal imprint upon all official documents, records and licenses.
(1963 Code)
CHAPTER 5
OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER
SECTION:
1-5-1: Official Newspaper Of The City
1-5-1: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER OF THE CITY:
The "Idahonian Daily News", a newspaper printed in the city of Moscow, is
hereby appointed, designated and constituted the official newspaper of the
city, and all ordinances, notices, statements and other writings required to be
published under and by virtue of the laws of the state and the government of
this city shall be given publication in said newspaper. (Ord. 293, 5-18-1987)
CHAPTER 6
SALARIES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Mayor And Council; Salaries
1-6-2: Salaries Of Appointive Officers
1-6-1: MAYOR AND COUNCIL; SALARIES:
   Commencing January 2, 2024, the salaries of the mayor and the members of the
city council shall be as follows:
   (A)   The mayor shall receive a monthly salary in the sum of seven hundred
dollars ($700.00).
   (B)   Each member of the council shall receive a monthly salary in the sum
of three hundred fifty dollars ($350.00).
(Ord. 394, 2-19-2013; amd. Ord. 394, 8-15-2023)
1-6-2: SALARIES OF APPOINTIVE OFFICERS:
Salaries of appointive officers shall be fixed by resolution of the council.
(1963 Code)
CHAPTER 7
PRECINCT
SECTION:
1-7-1: Precinct Description
1-7-2: Description To Be Filed
1-7-1: PRECINCT DESCRIPTION:
The city of Genesee, Idaho, shall be one precinct, described as follows:
Commencing at the northeast corner of section fourteen (14) in township thirty
seven (37) north, of range five (5) west of the B.M.; thence south along the
east line of section fourteen (14) to the southeast corner of Alder and Willow
Streets, as the same appears on record of the town of Genesee in the office of
the recorder of deeds in and for Latah County and State of Idaho; thence west
along the south line of Willow Street until it intersects the north and south
centerline of section fourteen (14), thence north along said center section
line until it intersects the south line of the right of way of the Spokane &
Palouse Railroad; thence along the south line of the said right of way until it
intersects the west line of section fourteen (14), thence north on the said
west line of section fourteen (14) to the northwest corner of said section
fourteen (14), thence east one-quarter (1/4) of a mile on the north line of
section fourteen (14), thence south one thousand one hundred and seventy feet
(1,170'), to the northwest corner of lot three (3) in block four (4) in the
west addition to the town of Genesee, as appears of record in the office of the
recorder of deeds in and for Latah County, Idaho; thence east to the north and
south centerline of section fourteen (14), thence north on said center section
line to the northwest corner of the northeast quarter of section fourteen (14)
thence east on the north line of said section fourteen (14) to the northeast
corner of said section 14, being the place of beginning.
(Ord. 243, 10-10-1977)
1-7-2: DESCRIPTION TO BE FILED:
The city clerk shall keep on file a description of the precinct or precincts.
Said description shall be amended by the clerk from time to time as directed by
resolution or other order of the city council. (Ord. 243, 10-10-1977)
CHAPTER 8
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-8-1: General Penalty Of The City
1-8-1: GENERAL PENALTY OF THE CITY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of the city may be fined
in a sum not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) for any offense and such
person may be confined in jail for a period of not more than six (6) months.
Either or both such fine and imprisonment may be imposed, and in addition
thereto, any person so convicted shall pay such costs as the court may assess.
Any person convicted of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of
intoxicating liquor or a narcotic drug may be fined in an amount not to exceed
three hundred dollars ($300.00) and may be confined in jail for not more than
six (6) months or both such fine and imprisonment.
The penalty herein provided shall be applicable to every ordinance of the city
the same as though it were a part of each and every separate ordinance. Any
person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of this city shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed committed for each
day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 213, 1-4-1971;
amd. 1982 Code)
CHAPTER 9
MAYOR
SECTION:
1-9-1: Mayor; Duties
1-9-2: Mayor To Sign Contracts
1-9-3: Qualifications And Term Of Office
1-9-4: Mayor May Grant Pardon (Rep. by 1982 Code)
1-9-5: Veto Power Of Mayor
1-9-6: Accounts And Reports Of Officers
1-9-7: Police Powers Of Mayor
1-9-8: Mayor May Require Aid
1-9-9: Other Powers
1-9-1: MAYOR; DUTIES:
The mayor shall devote so much of his time to the duties of his office as an
efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require. He shall, from time to
time, give the council such information and recommend such measures as he may
deem beneficial to the city. He shall examine the grounds of all complaints
against any of the officers of the city to determine existence of a violation
or neglect of duty, and report the evidence thereof, if deemed sufficient for
the removal of said officer, to the council. He shall require that every
officer, on the expiration of his term of office or resignation or removal from
the same, deliver to his successor all money, books, papers, maps, plats,
furniture, fixtures, apparatus, machinery, tools and instruments and
appurtenances belonging to such office. He shall perform all other duties
imposed on him by the laws of the state. (1963 Code)
1-9-2: MAYOR TO SIGN CONTRACTS:
The mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his name officially for and in
behalf of the city on all contracts, including deeds, bonds, bills, notes,
obligations and other agreements, documents and papers, to which the city is a
party, and to require that the conditions in the said instruments are
faithfully performed and to borrow money on the credit of the city when
authorized by the council. (1963 Code)
1-9-3: QUALIFICATIONS AND TERM OF OFFICE:
Any person shall be eligible to hold the office of mayor who is a qualified
elector of the city at the time of his election and remains a qualified elector
during his term of office. The term of office of mayor shall be for a period of
four (4) years. He shall take office at the time and in the manner provided for
installation of councilmen. (1982 Code)
1-9-4: MAYOR MAY GRANT PARDON:
(Rep. by 1982 Code)
1-9-5: VETO POWER OF MAYOR:
The mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the city
council, provided that any ordinance vetoed by the mayor may be passed over his
veto by a vote of one-half (1/2) plus one member of the full council,
notwithstanding the veto, and should the mayor neglect or refuse to sign any
ordinance and return the same with his objection, in writing, at the next
regular meeting of the council, the same shall become a law without his
signature. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code)
1-9-6: ACCOUNTS AND REPORTS OF OFFICERS:
The mayor shall have the power, when he deems it necessary, to require any
officer of the city to exhibit his accounts or other papers, and to make
reports to the council in writing touching any subject or matter he may require
pertaining to his office. (1963 Code)
1-9-7: POLICE POWERS OF MAYOR:
The mayor shall have jurisdiction over all places within five (5) miles of the
corporate limits of the city for the enforcement of any health or quarantine
ordinance and regulation thereof, and shall have jurisdiction in all matters,
excepting taxation, within one mile of the corporate limits. (1963 Code; amd.
1982 Code)
1-9-8: MAYOR MAY REQUIRE AID:
The mayor is hereby authorized to call on every male inhabitant in the city
over eighteen (18) years of age and under the age of fifty (50) years to aid in
enforcing the laws. (1963 Code)
1-9-9: OTHER POWERS:
The mayor shall have all other powers granted by the laws of the state. (1963
Code)
CHAPTER 10
CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-10-1: Duties Of Councilmen
1-10-2: Qualifications And Terms Of Office
1-10-3: Vacancies; Appointments
1-10-4: Time And Place Of Meetings
1-10-5: How To Conduct Council Meetings
1-10-6: Elect President Of The Council
1-10-7: Consent Calendar
1-10-1: DUTIES OF COUNCILMEN:
The members of the City Council, the legislative and policy making branch of
the government of the City, shall devote so much of their time to the duties of
their office as an efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require. They
shall attend all meetings of the Council, unless lawfully excused therefrom,
and perform all duties which by the nature of their office they should
reasonably perform. (1963 Code)
1-10-2: QUALIFICATIONS AND TERMS OF OFFICE:
The Council shall consist of four (4) members, one-half (1/2) of whom shall be
elected at each general City election. Any person shall be eligible to hold the
Office of Councilman of this City who is, at the time of election, and remains,
a qualified elector under the constitution and laws of the State. Each
Councilman elected at a general City election, except as otherwise specifically
provided, shall hold office for a term of four (4) years, and until his
successor is elected and qualified. Councilmen elected at each general City
election shall be installed at the first meeting in January following election.
The manner of conducting that meeting shall be as herein set forth and not
otherwise. The incumbents shall meet and conduct such business as may be
necessary to conclude fiscal matters of the preceding year; the newly elected
shall then subscribe to the oath of office, be presented certificates of
election, assume the duties of their position and conduct such business as
necessary, one item of which shall be the election of a member as President of
the Council. (1982 Code)
1-10-3: VACANCIES; APPOINTMENTS:
A vacancy on the Council shall be filled by appointment made by the Mayor with
the consent of the majority of the remaining Council, which appointee shall
serve only until the next general City election, at which time such vacancy
shall be filled for the balance of the original term. (1982 Code)
1-10-4: TIME AND PLACE OF MEETINGS:
The City Council shall hold regular sessions of the Council in the City Hall on
the first and on the third Tuesdays of each month at six o’clock (6:00) P.M.
(Ord. 406, 9-6-2016; amd. Ord. 419, 6-16-2020)
1-10-5: HOW TO CONDUCT COUNCIL MEETINGS:
There is hereby adopted by the City for the purpose of establishing rules and
regulations for the conduct of Council meetings, the Clerk's duties and the
Mayor's duties, in relation to Council meetings, the 1990 (ninth) edition of
"Robert's Rules of Order", newly revised, of which not less than one copy is
now on file in the Office of the City Clerk and the same is hereby adopted and
incorporated as fully as if set forth at length herein. (Ord. 346, 2-7-2000)
1-10-6: ELECT PRESIDENT OF THE COUNCIL:
At the time of taking office, the Council shall elect one of the members of the
Council, who shall be styled President of the Council, and who shall preside at
all meetings of the Council in the absence of the Mayor; and, in the absence of
the President, elect one of their own body to occupy his place temporarily, who
shall be styled Acting President of the Council, and the President and Acting
President, when occupying the place of Mayor, shall have the same privileges as
other members of the Council, and all acts of the President and Acting
President, while acting, shall be binding upon the Council and upon the City as
if done by the Mayor. (1963 Code)
1-10-7: CONSENT CALENDAR:
   (A)   When the Mayor determines that any item of business requires action by
the Council, but is of a routine and noncontroversial nature, he may cause such
item to be presented at a regular meeting of the Council as part of a consent
calendar.
   (B)   The consent calendar shall be introduced by a motion "to approve the
consent calendar", and shall be considered by the council as a single item.
   (C)   There shall be no debate or discussion by any member of the council
regarding any item on the consent calendar, beyond asking questions for simple
clarification.
   (D)   On objection by any member of the council to inclusion of any item on
the consent calendar, that item shall be removed from the consent calendar
forthwith. Such objection may be recorded at any time prior to the taking of a
vote on the motion to approve the consent calendar. All such items shall be
considered individually, in the order in which they were objected to,
immediately following consideration of the consent calendar.
   (E)   Approval of the motion to approve the consent calendar shall be fully
equivalent to approval, adoption, or enactment of each motion exactly as if
each had been acted upon individually.
   (F)   Approval of the motion must be made by roll call vote.
   (G)   The city clerk shall record in the council minutes each item passed
under the consent calendar individually and in full or, if possible,
separately. (Ord. 346, 2-7-2000)
CHAPTER 11
APPOINTIVE OFFICERS
SECTION:
1-11-1: Appointment By Mayor
1-11-2: Term Of Office And Removal
1-11-3: Appointments To Offices Hereafter Created
1-11-4: City Clerk, Duties; Journal; Administering Oaths
1-11-5: City Attorney, Duties
1-11-6: Treasurer, Duties; Record Of Outstanding Bonds
1-11-7: City Engineer; Duties
1-11-8: Bonds Of Officers
1-11-1: APPOINTMENT BY MAYOR:
The mayor, with the consent of the council, shall appoint a clerk, treasurer,
attorney, chief of police, chief of fire department and an engineer. (1963
Code; amd. 1982 Code)
1-11-2: TERM OF OFFICE AND REMOVAL:
All appointive officers shall hold office for the term for which they were
appointed and qualified; provided, that any appointive officer may, at any
time, be removed by the action of the mayor with the concurrence of a majority
of the council; provided, further, that all employees holding positions by
virtue of appointment without the approval of the city council, may be removed
or discharged at the pleasure of the appointing power. (1963 Code)
1-11-3: APPOINTMENTS TO OFFICES HEREAFTER CREATED:
The mayor, by and with the consent of the council, shall make appointments to
all city offices now existing which have not been in this chapter specifically
named and which may be hereafter created from time to time by the council.
(1963 Code)
1-11-4: CITY CLERK, DUTIES; JOURNAL; ADMINISTERING OATHS:
The city clerk shall keep a correct journal of the proceedings of the council
and shall have the custody of all laws and ordinances of the city. He may
administer oaths to any person concerning any matter submitted to him or the
city council. He shall also perform such other duties as may be required by
ordinance. (1982 Code)
1-11-5: CITY ATTORNEY, DUTIES:
The city attorney shall be the legal adviser of the council. He shall commence,
prosecute and defend all noncriminal suits or actions necessary on behalf of
the city, or that may be ordered by the council. When requested, he shall
attend meetings of the council and give them his opinion upon any matters
submitted to him. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code)
1-11-6: TREASURER, DUTIES; RECORD OF OUTSTANDING BONDS:
The treasurer of the city shall be the custodian of all monies belonging to the
city. He shall keep a separate account of each fund or appropriation, and the
debits and credits belonging thereto. He shall give a receipt to every person
paying money into the treasury, thereon specifying the date of payment and on
what account paid. He shall also file copies of such receipts with his monthly
reports. He shall, at the end of each and every month and as often as may be
required, render an account to the city council, under oath, showing the state
of the treasury at the date of such account and the balance of money in the
treasury. He shall also accompany such accounts with a statement of all
receipts and disbursements, together with all warrants redeemed and paid by
him, which said warrants, with any and all vouchers held by him, shall be filed
with his said account in the clerk's office, and if said treasurer neglect or
fail for the space of ten (10) days from the end of each and every month, to
render his said account, his office shall be declared vacant, and the city
council shall fill the vacancy by appointment. He shall also keep a record of
all outstanding bonds against the city, showing the number, amount of each and
to whom said bonds were issued; and when any bonds are purchased, paid or
canceled, said record shall show the fact. In his annual report, he shall
describe particularly the bonds issued and sold during the year and the terms
of the sale with each and every item of expense thereof. (1982 Code)
1-11-7: CITY ENGINEER, DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the city engineer to locate the lines and grades of all
streets, sidewalks, alleys, avenues and other public ways and to perform such
other services as may be required of him by statute, ordinance or the mayor and
council. (1963 Code)
1-11-8: BONDS OF OFFICERS:
The several officers herein named shall give bonds to the city with two (2) or
more sufficient sureties in the minimum penal sums as follows; provided, surety
bonds will be furnished at the expense of the city in lieu of personal bonds:
 
City clerk     $5,000.00
City treasurer 5,000.00
 
(1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code)
CHAPTER 12
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-12-1: Poll Hours
1-12-1: POLL HOURS:
The polls for all general and special city elections shall be open from eight
o'clock (8:00) A.M. Pacific Time and remain open until eight o'clock (8:00)
P.M. Pacific Time. (Ord. 363, 9-17-2003)
CHAPTER 13
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
SECTION:
1-13-1: Creation Of Right
1-13-2: Number Of Petitioners Required
1-13-3: Form Of Petition
1-13-4: Time For Filing Petitions
1-13-5: Printing Of Petition And Sheets For Signature; Time Limits For
Perfecting Petition
1-13-6: Verification On Sheets For Signatures
1-13-7: Examination And Certification Of Signatures
1-13-8: Sufficiency Of Petition; Notification; Effect Of Council Action;
Election
1-13-9: Form Of Ballot
1-13-10: Conduct Of Election
1-13-11: Costs Of Election
1-13-12: Canvass Of Returns
1-13-13: Prohibited Acts; Penalties
1-13-1: CREATION OF RIGHT:
The people of this city shall have the right to enact ordinances through the
initiative process, and to repeal ordinances through the referendum process,
according to the procedures set forth herein. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-2: NUMBER OF PETITIONERS REQUIRED:
To enact an ordinance by initiative or to repeal an ordinance by referendum,
there shall be attached or appended to the petition the signatures of the legal
voters of the city equal to at least twenty percent (20%) of the total number
of electors who cast votes at the last general election in the city. "General
election" shall mean the last municipal general election, held in odd numbered
years. (Ord. 349, 6-6-2001)
1-13-3: FORM OF PETITION:
The initiative petition shall be in substantially the following form:
Initiative Petition to the Mayor and Council of the City of Genesee, Idaho:
"We, the undersigned citizens and legal voters of the City of Genesee,
respectfully demand that the following proposed ordinance, to-wit: (setting out
full text of measure proposed) shall be submitted to the legal voters of the
City of Genesee, for their approval or rejection at an election to be called in
accordance with Idaho Code Section 50-501(3), and each for himself says: I have
personally signed this petition; I am a legal voter of the City of Genesee; my
residence and post office are correctly written after my name.
Name                      Street and Number          
   Post Office               
(Here follow numbered lines for signatures)
The petition for referendum on any ordinance passed by the city council shall
be in substantially the same form with appropriate title and changes, setting
out in full the text of the ordinance to be referred to the people for their
approval or rejection. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-4: TIME FOR FILING PETITIONS:
Referendum petitions with the requisite number of signatures attached shall be
filed with the city clerk not less than sixty (60) days following the final
adoption of the ordinance to be subject to referendum. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-5: PRINTING OF PETITION AND SHEETS FOR SIGNATURE; TIME LIMITS FOR
PERFECTING PETITION:
   (A)   Before or at the time of beginning to circulate any petition for
initiative or referendum, the person or persons, organization or organizations
under whose authority the petition is to be circulated, shall send or deliver
to the city clerk a copy of such petition duly signed by at least twenty (20)
electors eligible to sign such petition. The clerk shall immediately examine
the petition and specify the form and kind and size of paper on which the
petition shall be printed and circulated for further signatures. All petitions
and sheets for signatures shall be printed on a good quality bond or ledger
paper, on pages eight and one-half inches (81/2") in width by thirteen inches
(13") in length, with a margin of one and three-fourths inches (13/4") at the
top for binding, and the sheets for signatures shall have numbered lines
thereon from one to twenty (20) for signatures. The petition shall be prepared
in sections, with each section numbered consecutively. Each section of a
petition must have a printed copy of the petition as the first page, and each
section shall have attached to it not more than ten (10) sheets for signatures.
   (B)   The city clerk shall indicate in writing on the petition that he/she
has approved it as to form, the clerk shall inform the person or persons,
organization or organizations under whose authority the petition is to be
circulated, in writing, that the petition must be perfected with the required
number of certified signatures within sixty (60) days following the date of
approval as to form. Any petition that has not been perfected with the required
number of certified signatures within the sixty (60) days allowed shall be
declared null and void ab initio in its entirety. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-6: VERIFICATION ON SHEETS FOR SIGNATURES:
Each and every signature sheet of each petition containing signatures shall be
verified on the face thereof in substantially the following form by the person
who circulated said sheet of the petition, by his or her affidavit thereon, as
a part thereof:
State of Idaho   )
         ) ss.
   County of Latah    )
   I,                         , swear, under penalty of perjury, that every
person who signed this sheet of the foregoing petition signed his or name
thereto in my presence. I believe that each has stated his or name and the
accompanying required information on the signature sheet correctly, and that
the person was eligible to sign this petition.
         Signature                   
         Post Office Address           
Subscribed and sworn to before me this          day of              , 20     .
(Notary Seal)   Notary Public             
      Post Office Address           
(Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-7: EXAMINATION AND CERTIFICATION OF SIGNATURES:
   (A)   All petitions with attached signature sheets shall be presented on the
same day to the city clerk who shall make a cursory examination of them to
determine whether the petitions apparently contain the necessary number of
signatures.
      1.   If a total number of signatures on the petitions is not sufficient
to satisfy the number required by section
1-13-2 of this chapter, all petitions with attached signature sheets shall be
retained by the city clerk who shall notify in writing the person filing the
petition of the number of signatures needed, and further signatures may be
gathered, if within the time limit of section
1-13-5 of this chapter.
      2.   If the cursory examination of the signature sheets reveals:
         (a)   Erasures on any signature;
         (b)   Illegible or undecipherable signatures;
         (c)   Signatures not properly identified by all of the information
required on the sheet;
         (d)   Duplicate signatures;
         (e)   Signatures of persons who have requested in writing to have
their names removed from the petition;
the city clerk shall summarily reject such signatures and they shall not be
counted. Each rejected signature shall be drawn through with ink and initialed
by the clerk. If the total number of signatures not rejected is not sufficient
to satisfy the number required by section
1-13-2 of this chapter, all petitions with attached signature sheets shall be
retained by the clerk who shall notify in writing the person filing the
petition of the number of signatures needed, and further signatures may be
gathered, if within the time limit of section
1-13-5 of this chapter.
   (B)   All petitions presented to the city clerk found to apparently contain
the necessary number of signatures, after the cursory examination provided for
above, shall be filed with the city clerk and become public records of the city
not to be returned. The city clerk shall examine each such signature purported
to be that of a registered elector of the city, and compare each such signature
with the registration documents available to the city clerk. The city clerk
shall summarily reject all signatures which are not the signatures of a
registered elector of the city; and such signature shall be drawn through with
ink and initialed by the city clerk. The city clerk may take not to exceed ten
(10) days after filing of the petition to complete his/her examination. The
city clerk shall certify each signature found to comply with all of the
requirements of this chapter by an appropriate mark following each signature.
(Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-8: SUFFICIENCY OF PETITION; NOTIFICATION; EFFECT OF COUNCIL ACTION;
ELECTION:
   (A)   In the event that a petition filed with a city clerk does not contain
the required number of certified signatures, the city clerk shall inform the
person or organization under whose authority the petition was circulated that
the petition is defective for lack of certified signatures, and specify the
number of additional signatures required to make the petition valid. The
petition must be perfected within thirty (30) days of the date that the city
clerk finds the petition defective for lack of certified signatures. If the
petition is not perfected within the thirty (30) day period, the clerk shall
declare the petition null and void ab initio in its entirety.
   (B)   In the event that a petition filed with a city clerk is found by the
city clerk to contain the required number of certified signatures, the city
clerk shall promptly, by certified mail, inform the petitioners, and shall also
notify the city council at its next meeting that the initiative or referendum
petition is in proper form.
      1.   If the petition is for a referendum, the city council shall have
thirty (30) days from the day of certification of the petition to repeal the
ordinance being referred to the voters. In the event the council repeals the
ordinance, the referendum petition shall be declared null and void.
      2.   If the petition is an initiative petition, the city council shall
have thirty (30) days to pass an ordinance substantially as proposed by the
petition. In the event the council passes such an ordinance, the initiative
petition shall be null and void.
      3.   In the event the city council neither repeals the ordinance which is
the subject of a referendum petition, nor enacts an ordinance which is the
subject of an initiative petition, an election shall be ordered by the city
clerk to be conducted citywide. A special election for initiative or referendum
shall be provided not more than ninety (90) days following the certification of
the petition, provided that in the event a municipal election will occur within
the ninety (90) days, the initiative or referendum shall be submitted at the
time of the municipal election. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-9: FORM OF BALLOT:
The city council shall prepare a ballot for an initiative or referendum
election in one of the following ways:
   (A)   If the full text of the ordinance or proposed ordinance to be voted
upon does not exceed one hundred twenty (120) words in length, it may be set
out in full on the election ballot; or
   (B)   If the full text of the ordinance or proposed ordinance to be voted
upon exceeds one hundred twenty (120) words in length, and the council votes
not to have it printed at length on the election ballot, it shall, with the
assistance of the city attorney, prepare a short title and description of the
ordinance or proposed ordinance which shall clearly and impartially state its
purpose and effect, which short title and description shall be printed on the
election ballot. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-10: CONDUCT OF ELECTION:
Initiative or referendum elections, whether special or general, shall be
conducted and the results thereof canvassed and certified in all respects as
near as practicable, in like manner as general elections, except as otherwise
provided. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-11: COSTS OF ELECTION:
Upon the filing of any initiative or referendum petition with the city clerk,
petitioners shall post bond with the clerk in an amount sufficient to offset
the estimated expense of conducting the election, unless such election is to be
held at the time of a regular general municipal election. As near as
practicable after the election, the total actual expenses of the election shall
be tabulated by the city clerk. The petitioners shall be jointly and severally
liable for payment into the city treasury of the whole amount of the expenses
of such election. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-12: CANVASS OF RETURNS:
The mayor and council shall meet within five (5) days after said election to
canvass the votes cast at such election, and the city clerk shall immediately
announce the results. Any initiative measure approved by a majority of the
votes cast shall be in full force and effect from the date of such
announcement. Any ordinance which is the subject of a referendum receiving less
than a majority of the votes cast shall be repealed, effective on the date of
such announcement. (Ord. 348, 3-21-2001)
1-13-13: PROHIBITED ACTS; PENALTIES:
A person is guilty of a misdemeanor who:
   (A)   Signs any name other than his own on any initiative or referendum
petition;
   (B)   Knowingly signs his name more than once on the same initiative or
referendum petition;
   (C)   Knowingly signs his name to any initiative or referendum petition if
he is not a registered city elector;
   (D)   Wilfully or knowingly circulates, published or exhibits any false
statement or representation concerning the contents, purport or effect of any
initiative or referendum petition for the purpose of obtaining any signature to
any such petition, or for the purpose of persuading any person to sign any such
petition.
   (E)   Presents to any officer for filing any initiative or referendum
petition to which is attached, appended or subscribed any signature which the
person so filing such petition knows to be false or fraudulent, or not the
genuine signature of the person purporting to sign such petition, or whose name
is attached, appended or subscribed thereto;
   (F)   Circulates or causes to circulate any initiative or referendum
petition, knowing the same to contain false, forged or fictitious names;
   (G)   Makes any false affidavit concerning any initiative or referendum
petition or the signatures appended thereto;
   (H)   Offers, proposes or threatens for any pecuniary reward or
consideration, including, but not limited to:
      1.   Attempting to sell, hinder or delay any initiative or referendum
petition or any part thereof or any signatures thereon;
      2.   Desist from beginning, promoting or circulating any initiative or
referendum petition;
      3.   Attempting in any manner or form to use any recall petition or any
power of promotion or opposition in any manner or form for extortion, blackmail
or secret or private intimidation of any person or business interest. (Ord.
348, 3-21-2001)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
Planning And Zoning Commission   1
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Definitions
2-1-2: Creation Of Commission
2-1-3: Qualifications And Terms Of Office
2-1-4: Rules; Organization And Meetings
2-1-5: Duties
2-1-6: Maps; Plats And Replats
2-1-7: Employees And Expenditures
2-1-8: Acquisition Of Property
2-1-9: Severability
2-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter:
   APPOINTIVE MEMBERS: All other members of the planning and zoning commission.
   COMMISSION: The planning and zoning commission created by this chapter.
   EX OFFICIO MEMBERS: The members of the planning and zoning commission chosen
from among the officials or employees of the municipality.
   GOVERNING BODY: The mayor and council of the city of Genesee, Idaho. (Ord.
222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-2: CREATION OF COMMISSION:
There is hereby created an official planning and zoning commission to consist
of seven (7) members to be appointed by the mayor and confirmed by the council.
The commission may consist entirely of appointive members or of both appointive
members and ex officio members with not more than one-third (1/3) ex officio
members. (Ord. 222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-3: QUALIFICATIONS AND TERMS OF OFFICE:
Appointive members of the commission shall be eligible and registered voters of
the city, provided that one such appointive member may be a resident of the
area of city impact. The term of office for the ex officio members shall
correspond to their respective tenure of office as an official or employee of
the city. The term of office for the first appointive members of the commission
shall be two (2), four (4) and six (6) years, to be determined by lot and
thereafter the terms for each appointive member shall be six (6) years.
Vacancies occurring otherwise than through the expiration of terms shall be
filled by the mayor and confirmed by the council. Members may be removed after
a hearing before the council and by a majority vote of the council. Members
shall be selected without respect to political affiliation and shall serve
without compensation. (Ord. 292, 11-9-1973; amd. 1982 Code)
2-1-4: RULES; ORGANIZATION AND MEETINGS:
The commission shall elect its own chairman and create and fill such other
offices as it may determine it requires for the proper conduct of the affairs
and business of the commission. Meetings of the commission shall be held when
duly called by the chairman by written or oral notice. A majority of the
appointive members of the commission shall be necessary to constitute a quorum
at any meeting. All meetings shall be open to the public. Written rules
consistent with this chapter and the laws of the state of Idaho for the
transaction of business of the commission shall be adopted and a written record
of meetings, resolutions, findings and determinations shall be kept, which
record shall be public. (Ord. 222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-5: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the commission to recommend and make suggestions to the
governing body for the adoption of coordinated plans for the physical
development of the municipality, for the formation of zoning districts; to make
suggestions concerning the laying out, widening, extending and location of
streets, roads and highways for the relief of traffic; to make suggestions
concerning density of population and development of land; to make suggestions
concerning the future growth, development and beautification of said
municipality in respect to its public buildings, streets, parks, grounds and
lands in order to promote the public health, morals, safety and welfare of the
inhabitants of said municipality; to give suggestions and advice to individual
citizens concerning landscaping and location of buildings, structures of works
to be erected, constructed or altered by or for such individual. (Ord. 222, 11-
9-1973)
2-1-6: MAPS; PLATS AND REPLATS:
Any and all maps, plats and replats of lands which require the approval of the
governing body or of an officer or employee shall first be submitted to the
commission for its suggestions and the commission shall have a reasonable time,
to be fixed by the governing body, within which to examine such maps, plats or
replats before returning the same with its suggestions. (Ord. 222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-7: EMPLOYEES AND EXPENDITURES:
Any expenditures of the commission (exclusive of gifts) shall be within the
amounts appropriated and set aside by the governing body for the purposes of
the commission as set forth in this chapter. Within such limits the commission
is authorized to employ such employees and technical advisors as it deems
necessary for the accomplishment of its authorized purposes and work. (Ord.
222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-8: ACQUISITION OF PROPERTY:
The commission is authorized to acquire by gift, devise or bequest, lands and
other property in the name of the municipality to carry out the purposes of
this chapter. (Ord. 222, 11-9-1973)
2-1-9: SEVERABILITY:
The provisions of this chapter are hereby declared to be severable and if any
provision of this chapter or the application of such provision to any person or
circumstance is declared invalid for any reason, such declaration shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this chapter. (Ord. 222, 11-9-
1973)
TITLE 3
HEALTH AND SANITATION
Water Department And Regulations   1
Sewer Rates   2
Sewer Regulations   3
Solid Waste Disposal   4
Cross Connection Control   5
Water And Sewer Facilities   6
CHAPTER 1
WATER DEPARTMENT AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
3-1-1: Water Connections Required
3-1-2: Water Distributed Through Meters
3-1-3: Meter Connection Requirements
3-1-4: Charges Against Property Owner
3-1-5: Maintenance And Repair Of Meters
3-1-6: Time Of Meter Readings
3-1-7: Due Dates
3-1-8: Water Service Outside City Limits
3-1-9: Water System Property Of City
3-1-10: Water Use Regulations
3-1-1: WATER CONNECTIONS REQUIRED:
   (A)   Connection Standards: The water commissioner is hereby empowered and
it is hereby made his duty in all cases where there is city water available to
compel every owner or occupant where water is to be used on lands, buildings or
premises, fronting or abutting on streets, highways or alleys or within two
hundred feet (200') of the same in case of unplatted land, to construct or
cause to be constructed a water line connection which shall connect such lands,
buildings or premises within the nearest accessible city water line. The water
commissioner shall have power and authority to examine or cause to be examined,
all buildings as to plumbing fixtures and water connections thereof, and, when
in his judgment, the plumbing fixtures or water connections are found to be
defective or unsanitary, he shall have the power to order their removal, repair
or substitution and require them to be placed in a sanitary condition and he
shall thereupon give the owner or any person occupying any building or
premises, notice in writing specifying the time when any defective water
connection or unsanitary fixtures must be completed or corrected. The water
commissioner shall make a copy of such notice which shall be kept in the office
of the clerk and open to the inspection of the public during the hours of said
clerk's office. After the time fixed by the water commissioner for the
completion of said connection and repairs, the owner or occupant shall be held
responsible for refusal to comply with such notice. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff.
6-15-1974)
   (B)   Public Improvements:
      1.   Plans Must Be Approved; Engineering Costs: Plans must meet all
specifications of this chapter and be brought to and approved by the city
council before any work is done. Within thirty (30) days of completion of
construction, as built plans shall be provided to the city. Owner shall
reimburse the city for all engineering costs incurred by the city.
      2.   Street, Water And Sewer Extensions: Any owner seeking to develop
property within the city or seeking connection to the city water or sewer
system shall be responsible for paying for the extension of such facilities,
including streets and storm water facilities, to the property.
      3.   Additional Requirements: The city may require that water and sewer
lines be sized to provide services beyond the needs of the property being
developed. In such case, the city shall pay the incremental costs related to
increasing the size of the line.
   (C)   Water Facility Standards: Water lines within the city shall comply
with the following standards:
      1.   The Idaho standards for public works construction, 1999, published
by the Idaho standards for public works construction committee are hereby
adopted. Three (3) copies of these standards shall be on file with the city
clerk for public use.
      2.   Fire hydrants shall be constructed every four hundred feet (400').
      3.   All plans shall be subject to approval by the city's engineer.
   (D)   Inspection By City: No water line, sewer line or storm water pipe
shall be covered until it has been inspected by the city. The developer or
contractor shall provide at least twenty four (24) hours' notice to the city of
need for inspection. All public facilities shall be warranted by the developer
or contractor for a period of three (3) years after acceptance by the city.
(Ord. 343, 3-15-1999)
3-1-2: WATER DISTRIBUTED THROUGH METERS:
All property owners upon whose premises water is consumed (by owners, by
tenants or otherwise), must have a water meter to be furnished by the city, at
the expense of the property owner. Such meter shall be installed adjacent to
the private property line, within the public right of way. All city water used
therein or upon said premises shall pass through and be measured by said water
meter. The property owner shall be responsible for the maintenance of the
service line from where it crosses the property line, regardless of the
location of the water meter.
In the event that any property owner shall refuse to allow such meter to be
installed, refuses to pay for the same or refuses to pay for the metered water
used, it shall be the duty of the city supervisor to forthwith discontinue the
water from the premises of such owner and/or property. (Ord. 387, 1-17-2012)
3-1-3: METER CONNECTION REQUIREMENTS:
Each residence and business establishment to which water is supplied by the
city, whether inside or outside the city limits, must have a separate meter
connection directly to the main, excepting, however, those portions of
buildings used principally for office or apartments where the property owner
furnishes water supplied to the tenants. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
3-1-4: CHARGES AGAINST PROPERTY OWNER:
   (A)   Water Meter: Before a meter is installed, the property owner shall pay
the city treasurer the cost of said meter together with the cost of
installation thereof, as billed.
   (B)   Tapping Application And Fee: Every person desiring city water must
make application to the clerk for permission to tap the city mains. Said
application to describe the property to be served, purposes for which water is
required, and illustrate the location of the desired tap (this may be
accomplished in conjunction with the building permit application).
Upon payment of the "tapping fee" of five hundred dollars ($500.00), which fee
must accompany the application, the city will have the main tapped and water
brought to the outer curb on the property line of the property indicated.
The following fees are enacted for new service hook-up:
 
Water
Water Connection And Tapping Fee: $10,000.00
Meter and Materials:              Cost + 10%
 
 
Sewer
Sewer Connection fee: $10,000.00
Tapping fee:          $2,000.00
Total:                $12,000.00
 
   (C)   Water Rates: When a meter has been installed, water will not
thereafter be supplied to the premises of such property except upon metered
water rates to be paid by the property owner or tenant for all water used upon
said premises, whether by himself, tenant or otherwise. Property owner is
primarily responsible for payment of water charges.
The following rates are hereby established as the official water rates of the
city for the following types of water uses:
      1.   Types Of Water Uses:
      Single residence.
      Duplex residence - per unit.
      Multiple residence - per unit.
      Dwelling units located in single residences or in commercial business
establishments - per unit.
      Mobile home parks - per unit.
      Commercial business establishments - per unit.
      Public and private schools.
      2.   Rates Inside And Outside City:
         (a)   User Fee: The following monthly water user fees are hereby
enacted:
            (1)   The minimum water user fee for all users connected to the
City's water system will increase twenty-five dollars ($25.00) per month, from
ten dollars and ninety-four cents ($10.94) to thirty-five dollars and ninety-
four cents ($35.94) per month effective November 1, 2020.
            (2)   Residents who qualify for the Latah County Circuit Breaker
Program or the Veterans Property Tax Reduction Program will have a fifteen
dollars ($15.00) per month increase from ten dollars and ninety-four cents
($10.94) to twenty-five dollars and ninety-four cents ($25.94) per month
effective November 1, 2020.
         (b)   Minimum Rate: The following monthly water rates are hereby
enacted:
            (1)   The minimum user fee for all users connected to the City's
water system is ten dollars and ninety-four cents ($10.94) per month, (fifty-
two cents ($0.52) increase over the ten dollars and forty-two cents ($10.42)
current charge) with the charges for residential usage assessed at the
following rates:
               a.   Ten dollars and fifty cents ($10.50) per month for the
first one thousand (1,000) gallons or less; plus
               b.   Seventy-five cents ($0.75) per one thousand (1,000) gallons
for the next four thousand (4,000) gallons; plus
               c.   Eighty-two and a half cents ($0.82½) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next five thousand (5,000) gallons; plus
               d.   Ninety cents ($0.90) per one thousand (1,000) gallons for
the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               e.   One dollars and twenty cents ($1.20) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               f.   One dollars and thirty-five cents ($1.35) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for each additional 1,000 gallons in excess of thirty thousand
(30,000) gallons.
            (2)   The charges for commercial usage is assessed at the following
rates:
               a.   Ten dollars and fifty cents ($10.50) per month for the
first one thousand (1,000) gallons or less; plus
               b.    Seventy-five cents ($0.75) per one thousand (1,000)
gallons for the next four thousand (4,000) gallons; plus
               c.    Eighty-two and a half cents ($0.82 ½) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next five thousand (5,000) gallons; plus
               d.   Ninety cents ($0.90) per one thousand (1,000) gallons for
the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               e.   One dollars and twenty cents ($1.20) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next thirty thousand (30,000) gallons; plus
               f.   One dollar and thirty-five cents ($1.35) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for each additional one thousand (1,000) gallons in excess of
fifty thousand (50,000) gallons.
            (3)   The charges for residential users connected to the city's
water system outside the city limits are assessed as follows:
               a.   Twenty-one dollars ($21.00) per month for the first one
thousand (1,000) gallons or less; plus
               b.   Seventy-five cents ($0.75) per one thousand (1,000) gallons
for the next four thousand (4,000) gallons; plus
               c.   Eighty-two and a half cents ($0.82 ½) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next 5,000 gallons; plus
               d.   Ninety cents ($0.90) per one thousand (1,000) gallons for
the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               e.   One dollars and twenty cents ($1.20) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               f.   One dollar and thirty-five cents ($1.35) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for each additional one thousand (1,000) gallons in excess of
thirty thousand (30,000) gallons
            (4)   The charges for commercial users connected to the City's
water system outside the city limits are assessed as follows:
               a.    Twenty-one dollars ($21.00) per month for the first one
thousand (1,000) gallons or less; plus
               b.   Seventy-five cents ($0.75) per one thousand (1,000) gallons
for the next four thousand (4,000) gallons; plus
               c.   Eighty-two and a half cents ($0.82 ½) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next five thousand (5,000) gallons; plus
               d.   Ninety cents ($0.90) per one thousand (1,000) gallons for
the next ten thousand (10,000) gallons; plus
               e.   One dollars and twenty cents ($1.20) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for the next thirty thousand (30,000) gallons; plus
               f.   One dollar and thirty-five cents ($1.35) per one thousand
(1,000) gallons for each additional one thousand (1,000) gallons in excess of
fifty thousand (50,000) gallons.
      3.   Nonmetered Water Uses: Nonmetered water uses will be charged a
minimum rate of five dollars ($5.00) per month for each individual mobile home
in the park. One thousand (1,000) gallons of water will be deducted from the
total metered usage for each mobile home so charged and the remaining gallonage
will be charged at the above rates. The mobile home park owner is primarily
responsible for payment of water charges.
      4.   Rate Changes: All charges and rates established in this section may
be changed from time to time as deemed necessary and proper, by resolution duly
adopted at a regular or special meeting of the city council.
      5.   Direct Charge To Tenant: At the request of the property owner the
city shall directly charge the tenant of rented dwelling units, spaces or
business property the user fee. The property owner shall inform the city clerk
at city hall in writing of all changes in the names and addresses of tenants to
be charged directly and all changes of status as to occupancy or vacancy of
rental units, spaces or business properties within forty eight (48) hours of
such changes. In the event the required notice is not given to the city clerk
the owner shall be responsible for all water charges reflected by the most
recent information given to the city clerk.
      6.   Vacancies: No user fee or minimum rate shall be charged for any
period of time during which a rental dwelling unit, space or business property
is vacant, provided proper notice of such vacancy is given to the city clerk.
(Ord. 263, 12-8-1980; amd. Res. 2017-3, 8-15-2017; Res. 2019-5, 9-3-2019; Res.
2020-8, 10-6-2020; Res. 2022-3, 5-17-2022)
3-1-5: MAINTENANCE AND REPAIR OF METERS:
The city will repair or replace all defective meters with no cost to the
property owner, except in those instances where the meter has been damaged by
reason of the negligence of the water user, or by reason of the defective
condition of the plumbing on the premises of the water user, or by reason of
the backing up of hot water from the premises of the water user.
   (A)   Meter Damage; Liability: When any water meter has been damaged by
reason of the negligence of the user of city water, or by reason of the
defective condition of the plumbing on the premises of the water user, or by
reason of the backing up of hot water from the premises of the water user, then
such water user shall be liable and punishable under the provisions of section
1-8-1 of this code, and must pay for the replacement or repair of said meter in
an amount to be determined by the city council.
   (B)   Requirements After Repairs For Turning On Water: Whenever the city
supervisor is called upon to repair or replace a meter which has been damaged
as set forth in subsection (A) of this section, he may, at his discretion,
refuse to repair or replace said meter, and disconnect the water service line
to said premises; and may, by reason of defective plumbing on the premises of
the water user, refuse to reconnect the same until a check valve is installed
between the water meter and the premises on which water is used, in order to
prevent the water from backing up from said premises.
The city supervisor may require that a safety relief valve or "pop off" be
placed in service to relieve pressure on the hot water tank or other plumbing
fixtures located upon said premises. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
3-1-6: TIME OF METER READINGS:
The city supervisor shall commence reading all water meters on the twenty fifth
day of each month and shall continue to continuously read the same until all
the water meters have been read; excepting that, during the winter months, the
monthly usage will be estimated, as directed by the council. (Ord. 304, 12-4-
1989)
3-1-7: DUE DATES:
All water charges for water consumed shall be due and payable to the city
clerk/treasurer between the first day and the fifteenth day of each month. In
the event payment is not timely made, the following procedure shall be
conducted: (Ord. 286, 3-10-1986)
   (A)   Late Charge Added: On the first business day following the last day of
timely payment the city clerk/treasurer shall add a late charge of ten dollars
($10.00) to the unpaid balance which each user shall pay in addition to the
amount of the water charges then due. (Ord. 361, 3-19-2003)
   (B)   Identification Of Unpaid Charges: On the first business day following
the last day for timely payment, the city clerk/treasurer shall identify all
users whose water charges and late charges remain unpaid.
   (C)   Notice Of Delinquency Mailed: On the first business day following the
last day for timely payment, the city clerk/treasurer shall cause a notice of
delinquency to be mailed to each user whose water charges and late charges
remain unpaid. The notice of delinquency shall include the name of the user, a
statement that the water charges have not been paid, and the amount of the
payment due including the late charge. (Ord. 304, 12-4-1989)
   (D)   Identification Of Unpaid Charges After Mailing Delinquency Notice: On
the fifteenth day of the month, following the mailing of a notice of
delinquency, the city clerk/treasurer shall make a list of all users whose
water charges remain unpaid after being mailed a notice of delinquency during
the previous month. (Ord. 286, 3-10-1986)
   (E)   Shutoff Notice: On the sixteenth day of the month, following the
service of the notice of delinquency, the city clerk/treasurer shall cause to
be mailed to the nonpaying user and to the owner of the premises occupied by
said user, if the user is not also the owner, notice of shutoff of service. A
notice of shutoff will also be posted on the premises forty eight (48) hours
before shutoff occurs. The shutoff notice shall include the following:
      1.   The name of the user;
      2.   A statement that the water charges have not been paid;
      3.   The amount of payment due including the late charges;
      4.   A statement that unless the full amount due is paid on or before the
shutoff date, or unless the user has notified the city clerk/treasurer, in
person or in writing, that they will be present at the next city council
meeting, the water service will be discontinued and the water will be shut off;
      5.   A statement that if the water is shut off it will not be turned on
until the past due water charges, including the late charge, plus a charge of
seven dollars fifty cents ($7.50) for reinstatement of water service and a
deposit of thirty dollars ($30.00) as security for the payment of future water
charges are paid in full. (Ord. 361, 3-19-2003)
   (F)   Request For Hearing: Any owner who has received a shutoff notice may
contact the city clerk/treasurer, before the last day of the month in which
they received such notice, and request to be placed on the agenda of the next
regular meeting of the city council for the purpose of requesting that they be
heard by the city council as to any reasons that their water shall not be shut
off. The request to be placed on the agenda of such regular meeting shall delay
the shutting off of such owner's water until such time as such regular meeting
is held. After hearing such owner regarding the reasons that their water shall
not be shut off, the city council may allow such person additional time to make
payment or to take other action deemed appropriate by the city council.
   (G)   Identification Of Unpaid Charges After Mailing Shutoff Notice: On the
first day of each month the city clerk/treasurer shall prepare a list of all
users who have been mailed a shutoff notice and who have either failed to pay
the charges, or failed to request a hearing at the next council meeting. The
city clerk/treasurer shall deliver said list to the city supervisor who shall
cause the water service of each such user to be discontinued by shutting off
the water to the user. (Ord. 286, 3-10-1986; amd. Ord. 361, 3-19-2003)
   (H)   Reinstatement Of Service: Any user whose water service has been
discontinued for nonpayment of water charges shall have water service
reinstated upon the payment of all past due water charges, plus the late
charges, and a charge of seven dollars fifty cents ($7.50) for reinstatement of
water service, and upon the deposit of the sum of thirty dollars ($30.00) as
security for the payment of future water charges. (Ord. 286, 3-10-1986)
   (I)   Rate Changes: All changes and rates established in this section may be
changed from time to time as deemed necessary and proper, by resolution duly
adopted at a regular or special meeting of the city council. (Ord. 361, 3-19-
2003)
3-1-8: WATER SERVICE OUTSIDE CITY LIMITS:
In the event of need and/or at the discretion of the council, any service
outside the city limits may be terminated, upon notice, at any time by order of
the council. The fixing of water rates by the council for water service outside
the city is not to be read as imposing a duty upon the city to make such water
service available. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
3-1-9: WATER SYSTEM PROPERTY OF CITY:
All mains, laterals, pipes, hydrants and fixtures now laid, constructed or
installed or hereafter to be laid, constructed or installed in, under, across
or through the streets, avenues, alleys and other thoroughfares of the city or
easement rights of way granted to the city or adjacent territory, for supplying
water to said city and the inhabitants thereof are hereby declared to be the
property of the city, under the control thereof and subject to the provisions
of this chapter. No person or persons will be allowed to claim the right to
exclusive use of any such water line. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
3-1-10: WATER USE REGULATIONS:
Upon making application to the city for water use, each user hereby agrees to
the following additional regulations:
   (A)   The city reserves the right at any time to cut off water in the main
without notice. (Ord. 225, 6-10-1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
   (B)   When two (2) or more tenants occupy the same dwelling unit, the water
charges will be charged to one person only. (Ord. 263, 12-8-1980)
   (C)   No person or family supplied with water will be permitted to use it
for any other purpose than that stated in the agreement or to supply water in
any other way to other families or person.
   (D)   No alteration or extension shall be made in any water pipe, cock or
fixture without obtaining a permit therefor from the clerk. (Ord. 225, 6-10-
1974, eff. 6-15-1974)
   (E)   The city shall not be held liable under any circumstances for any
damages resulting from a deficiency or failure of water, whether by shutting
off the water to make repairs or connections, or by shutting off the water due
to the nonpayment of water charges, or for any other cause whatsoever. (Ord.
277)
   (F)   It shall be unlawful for any person to waste water or allow it to be
wasted by imperfect or leaking stops, valves, pipes, closets, faucets or other
fixtures or to use water closets without self-closing valves. If such waste of
water continues after receipt of notice from the city supervisor to make
repairs and to desist from the waste of water, the city supervisor shall shut
off the water supply from such premises until the necessary repairs have been
made. (Ord. 263, 12-8-1980)
   (G)   A water user who has had his water service discontinued for failure to
pay water charges shall be charged seven dollars fifty cents ($7.50) to have
water service restored and such water users shall also deposit with the city
the sum of thirty dollars ($30.00) as security for the payment of future water
charges which sum shall be applied against subsequent unpaid water charges
before a notice of delinquency is issued. The deposit of thirty dollars
($30.00) shall be refunded to the depositor after one year of timely payment of
all water charges. (Ord. 286, 3-10-1986)
   (H)   A water user who requests the city supervisor to turn off his water
for any reason whatsoever, will be charged seven dollars fifty cents ($7.50) to
have the water turned on. (Ord. 263, 12-8-1980)
CHAPTER 2
SEWER RATES
SECTION:
3-2-1: Sewer Rates Established
3-2-2: Charges; When Due
3-2-1: SEWER RATES ESTABLISHED:
   (A)   The following monthly sewer user fees are hereby enacted: The minimum
sewer user fee for all users connected to the City's sewer system will increase
ten dollars ($10.00) per month, from twelve dollars and thirteen cents ($12.13)
to twenty-two dollars and thirteen cents ($22.13) per month for the months of
Oct., Nov., Dec. 2018, Jan., Feb., and March 2019.
   (B)   The minimum sewer user fee for all users connected to the City's sewer
system will increase an additional ten dollars ($10.00) per month, from twenty-
two dollars and thirteen cents ($22.13) to thirty-two dollars and thirteen
cents ($32.13) per month beginning April 2019.
   (C)   Residents who qualify for the Latah County Circuit Breaker Program or
the Veterans Property Tax Reduction Program will have a two dollars ($2.00) per
month increase from the current twelve dollars and thirteen cents ($12.13)
sewer fee. The new rate of fourteen dollars and thirteen cents ($14.13) will be
in effect for the months Oct., Nov., Dec. 2018, Jan., Feb. and March 2019.
   (D)   Residents who qualify for the Latah County Circuit Breaker Program or
the Veterans Property Tax Reduction Program will have an additional two dollars
($2.00) fee increase beginning April, 2019. The new rate of sixteen dollars and
thirteen cents ($16.13) will be in place at that time.
   (E)   Genesee School District will have a flat fee for the sewer user fee of
two hundred and fifty dollars ($250.00) per month. This new rate will take
effect Oct. 1, 2018.
   (F)   The following monthly sewer project fees are hereby enacted: The
minimum sewer project fee for all users connected to the City's sewer system is
ninteen dollars and forty-five cents ($19.45) per month. (Ord. 262, 12-8-1980;
amd. Ord. 302, 10-2-1989; Res. 2018-5-B, 8-21-2018)
3-2-2: CHARGES; WHEN DUE:
All sewer charges shall be charged and paid with and subject to the same
procedures as water charges, as stated in sections
 3-1-6 and
3-1-7 of this title. The late charge established in subsection
3-1-7(A) of this title shall be applied to any delinquency in the combined
charging system but shall not be applied twice in the event of a delinquency in
both the water charges and the sewer charges. (Ord. 304, 12-4-1989)
CHAPTER 3
SEWER REGULATIONS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Purpose
3-3-2: Definitions
3-3-3: Use Of Public Sewer System Required
3-3-4: Connections To System
3-3-5: Sewer Construction Specifications And Inspections
3-3-6: Right To Enter Premises For Inspection
3-3-7: Sewer Fees
3-3-8: Injury To Sewerage System Unlawful
3-3-9: Unpolluted Water Discharges
3-3-10: Prohibited Discharges
3-3-11: Harmful Or Industrial Wastes
3-3-12: Private Sewer Repair Permit Required
3-3-13: Violations And Penalties
3-3-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to promote the public welfare by regulating and
limiting the type of sewage, including industrial waste, that may be discharged
into the city public sewers and storm drains; and authorizing a schedule of
rates and charges for services afforded by the city, revised periodically to
reflect actual operation, maintenance, replacement and debt service costs.
(Ord. 268, 7-6-1982)
3-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
Terms used in this chapter shall have the meanings herein given to them:
   APPROVING AUTHORITY: The city council or the sewer and water commissioner of
the city or his duly authorized deputy, agent or representative.
   BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND OR BOD: The quantity of oxygen, expressed in parts
per million by weight, utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter
under standard laboratory determinations made in accordance with procedures set
forth in "Standard Methods", for five (5) days' BOD determination.
   CITY: The city of Genesee, Idaho.
   DWELLING UNIT: A building or structure including mobile home, designed and/
or used for independent living quarters or residential purposes for family or
household use, including single, duplex or multiple structures howsoever
designed or constructed. Dwelling unit shall include boarding house and/or
lodging house where bed and board are provided for five (5) or more persons for
compensation.
   GARBAGE: The residue from the preparation and dispensing of food, and from
the handling, storage and sale of food products and produce.
   GROUND GARBAGE: The residue from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of
food that has been shredded to such degree that all particles will be carried
freely in suspension under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") in any dimension.
   HOUSE SERVICE LINE: The extension from the building drain to the public
sewer and is sometimes referred to as a service connection.
MG: Million gallons.
   MOBILE HOMES: See definition of Manufactured Home in section
 10-2-2 of this code.
   NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other
body of surface or ground water.
   PARTS PER MILLION: A weight to weight ratio; the parts per million value
multiplied by the factor eight and three hundred forty five-thousandths (8.345)
shall be equivalent to pounds per million gallons of water.
   PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation,
group or other entity.
pH: The logarithm (base 10) of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration
expressed in moles per liter and is a measure of the acidity or alkalinity of a
solution.
   PRIVATE SEWER: A sewer serving one or more buildings, residences or
properties, constructed by private contract.
   PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer provided by or subject to the jurisdiction of the
