6-5-8: License Fees
6-5-9: Revocation Of License
6-5-10: Penalties
6-5-11: Additional Remedies
6-5-12: Liability Of Parents
6-5-13: Appeals From Orders Of Destruction
6-5-14: Fees By Resolution
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 10, chapter 19 of this code.
6-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
For purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have the
meanings assigned to them herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words
used in the singular includes the plural. The word "shall" as used herein, is
always mandatory and not merely discretionary. The masculine includes the
feminine.
   ALLOW: To permit by neglecting to restrain or prevent.
   ALTERED ANIMAL: Male or female animals rendered incapable of producing
offspring.
   ANIMAL: Every nonhuman species of animal, both domesticated and wild,
including, but not limited to, dogs, cats, livestock and fowl.
   ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER: Any person designated as such by the city council
for the purpose of enforcing the provisions of this chapter.
   ANIMAL SHELTER: Any premises designated by the city for the purpose of
impounding and caring for animals held under the authority of this chapter.
   ANIMAL UNDER CONTROL: An animal secured by a leash or lead not exceeding
eight feet (8') in length; or is within eight feet (8') and under voice or sign
control of a responsible person; or is confined within a vehicle.
   AT LARGE: Off the premises of the owner and not under control of the owner
or another responsible person.
   BITE: Any aggressive or voluntary closure by an animal's mouth causing
either redness, breaking or tearing of the skin of any person, or which damages
or destroys the personal property of another.
   CRUELTY: Any act, omission or neglect whereby unnecessary or unjustifiable
physical or mental pain or suffering is caused or permitted, including failure
to provide proper drink, air, space, shelter or protection from the elements,
veterinary care, or nutritious food in sufficient quantities, with respect to
an animal. In the case of an activity in which physical pain is necessarily
caused, such as food processing, hunting, ranching, or pest elimination,
cruelty shall mean the failure to employ the most reasonable humane method
available under the circumstances.
   DANGEROUS ANIMAL: Any animal which attacks, bites, or injures human beings
or domesticated animals without adequate provocation, or which, because of
temperament, conditioning, or training, has a known propensity to attack, bite,
or injure human beings or domesticated animals. An animal which has previously
attacked or bitten any human or other animal without adequate provocation may
be deemed to be a dangerous animal.
   HARBORING: The keeping of any animal. The occupant of any premises on which
an animal remains, or to which it customarily returns daily for food and care,
for five (5) consecutive days or more is presumed to be harboring or keeping
the animal for the purposes of this chapter.
   KENNEL, COMMERCIAL: Any lot or premises or portion thereof, other than a
veterinary hospital or animal shelter, on which animals are maintained,
harbored, possessed, boarded, bred or cared for in return for compensation or
kept for sale.
   LIVESTOCK: Any animal normally kept for breeding, product or work including,
but not limited to, cow, calf, ox, steer, bull, horse, mare, colt, stallion,
mule, jack, jenny, hog, pig, goat, kid, llama, sheep, lamb, rabbit or guinea
pig.
   OWNER, CUSTODIAN OR KEEPER: Any person, including any firm, association,
partnership or corporation or their agents, or persons acting with their
permission, owning, keeping or harboring an animal.
   PREMISES: All of the real property under a person's or persons' ownership,
lease or control inside the inner line of a sidewalk; or if there is no
sidewalk, inside the curb, ditch or shoulder marking the edge of the traveled
or used portion of the public right of way. "Premises" also includes a motor
vehicle.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE ANIMAL: Any animal which unreasonably: a) annoys humans, b)
endangers the life or health of other animals or person, c) gives offense to
human senses, or d) which substantially interferes with the rights of citizens
other than its owner, to enjoyment of life or property. The term "public
nuisance animal" shall mean and include, but is not limited to, any animal
which:
   (A)   Is repeatedly found at large; or
   (B)   Damages the property of anyone other than its owner; or
   (C)   Chases vehicles; or
   (D)   Excessively makes disturbing noises, including, but not limited to,
continued and repeated howling, barking, whining, or other utterances causing
unreasonable annoyance, disturbance, or discomfort to neighbors or others; or
   (E)   Causes fouling of the air by odor and causing thereby unreasonable
annoyance or discomfort to neighbors or others; or
   (F)   Causes unsanitary conditions in enclosures or other surroundings where
the animal is kept or harbored; or
   (G)   By virtue of the number or types of animals maintained, is offensive
or dangerous to the public health, safety, or welfare; or
   (H)   Attacks other domestic animals.
   WILD ANIMAL: Any live monkey or ape, raccoon, skunk, fox, snake or other
reptile, leopard, wolf, coyote, panther, tiger, bear, lion, lynx or any other
animal or any bird of prey which can normally be found in a wild state. (Ord.
350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-2: ANIMAL CONTROL REGULATIONS:
   (A)   Keeping Animals In General:
      1.   No person who owns, keeps, maintains or harbors an animal shall
permit such animal to be or become a "public nuisance animal" (as defined in
section
6-5-1 of this chapter), to scatter garbage, refuse or debris, or to deposit
fecal material on any property not that of its owner or custodian without the
owner or custodian immediately removing it.
      2.   No person or household shall own, harbor or keep more than four (4)
dogs and/or four (4) cats over the age of six (6) months. Current residents in
possession of more than four (4) dogs and/or four (4) cats may, within thirty
(30) days of the adoption of ordinance 327, register such animals with the city
clerk by providing the clerk with the number and description of such animals
owned or kept on the date of adoption of ordinance 327 and those specific
animals shall be exempt from the above stated number limitation until their
death or other disposition. This limit shall not apply to any animal shelter,
veterinary hospital, commercial kennel, or pet shop.
      3.   No owner or custodian shall permit any animal owned by him or under
his control to run at large in or on any public property, vacant lot, or
unenclosed private property not that of the owner in the city.
      4.   Any animal found running at large may be taken up and impounded.
      5.   A cat shall not be deemed to be at large unless it is causing a
disturbance, or is a nuisance, or has been complained of, or is sick, injured
or obviously uncared for.
      6.   No owner or custodian shall permit any animal owned by him or under
his control to be upon the premises of another without the consent of the owner
of such premises.
      7.   No person shall keep, harbor or maintain an animal or animals within
the city in such a manner that the keeping of the same results in a nauseous,
foul or offensive condition.
      8.   No owner or custodian of an animal shall fail to provide it with
adequate food, water, shelter and necessary veterinary care which shall include
a current rabies vaccination.
      9.   Rabies vaccinations shall not be required for animals not normally
so immunized, nor for dogs and cats under six (6) months of age, nor where a
written statement from a licensed veterinarian indicates that such vaccination
would be injurious to the animal's health.
      10.   No person shall allow an animal to ride in the back of a pickup
truck upon a public roadway unless the bed is covered by a canopy or unless the
animal is confined or secured in such a manner that it cannot jump or fall out.
      11.   No person shall beat, torment, torture, cruelly ill treat or abuse
any animal.
      12.   No person who owns, keeps or harbors an animal shall abandon the
same. The delivery of a sick animal to a veterinarian for humane euthanasia, or
to the animal shelter for disposition shall not be considered abandonment.
      13.   Every animal in heat shall be confined in a building in such a
manner that such female animal cannot come in contact with another animal
except for planned breeding. This does not apply to livestock operations.
   (B)   Dangerous Animals:
      1.   No person shall keep or harbor within the city a "dangerous animal"
(as defined in section
6-5-1 of this chapter), unless such animals are restrained by a cage, fence, or
other adequate means from contact with the general public or with persons who
enter the premises with the actual or implied permission of the owner or
occupant and from any children who may wander onto the property; furthermore,
that notices of the presence of such animal are conspicuously displayed,
whereby the same may be seen by passing persons within the vicinity where such
animal may be kept, (and such additional conditions as may be imposed by the
city council, the animal control officer, or any court of competent
jurisdiction).
      2.   The owner of a dangerous animal shall consent to periodic
inspections by the animal control officer, city council or its designee.
      3.   A dangerous animal shall not be upon any roadway or public place
except while securely restrained, humanely muzzled if appropriate to the
species, and in the charge of a responsible person.
      4.   Any animal which has attacked or bitten any person or other animal,
without adequate provocation, may be seized by any police officer, animal
control officer or other citizen. Upon establishment, to the satisfaction of
any court of competent jurisdiction, of the vicious character of the animal,
said animal may be destroyed by a police officer or other agent of the city,
county, or state.
      5.   Provided, however, this section shall not apply to animals under the
control of a law enforcement or military agency.
      6.   No owner may keep a dangerous dog without a certificate of
registration issued under this chapter. The certificate of registration shall
be acquired within fourteen (14) days from the incident giving rise to the
classification, within fourteen (14) days of such animal being brought into the
city or within fourteen (14) days of termination of any criminal action. The
animal control authority of the city shall issue a certificate of registration
to the owner of a dangerous dog upon payment of the fee set forth herein,
provided the owner presents evidence of the restrains and notices enumerated in
this section.
      7.   Any person owning or harboring a dangerous animal shall be strictly
liable for damages caused by such animal.
   (C)   Kennels:
      1.   No person shall operate or maintain a kennel, except as authorized
by the zoning ordinance, within the city of Genesee, without first obtaining a
license therefor.
      2.   All kennels shall be maintained in a clean and sanitary manner,
provide adequate food and water, maintain temperatures suitable and comfortable
for every species of animal housed therein, provide cages of sufficient size to
allow each animal to stand up, turn around and stretch out to its full length,
provide for removal of feces and urine as often as necessary, but in no case
less often than daily, and provide for adequate veterinary care.
      3.   Periodic inspections by the animal control officer or mayor or his
designee shall be made of all kennel facilities.
   (D)   Pet Shops: No person shall operate or maintain a kennel which is a pet
shop, except as authorized by the zoning ordinance, within the city of Genesee,
without first obtaining a license therefor.
   (E)   Wild Animals:
      1.   No person shall keep or permit to be kept on his premises any wild
animal for display or exhibition purposes. This shall not be construed to apply
to humane research programs, zoological parks, or circuses.
      2.   No person shall keep or permit to be kept, any wild animal as a pet,
unless a permit has been granted by the director of the departments of fish and
game of the state for said animal. The animal control officer is authorized to
require such person to provide such secure enclosures and safeguards as are
necessary to protect residents from injury and ensure the peaceful enjoyment of
their property.
      3.   Any person owning or harboring any wild animal shall be strictly
liable for damages caused by such animal.
   (F)   Livestock And Fowl:
      1.   No person shall keep or maintain any livestock or fowl within the
city, except as authorized by the zoning ordinance 1 .
      2.   Every person keeping or maintaining livestock and fowl within the
city shall keep and maintain the same in a clean and sanitary condition, shall
at all times comply with the sanitary regulations imposed by the animal control
officer, and shall not permit such livestock or fowl to become or remain public
nuisance animals.
      3.   No person shall permit any livestock or fowl to be at large in or
upon any street, avenue, alley or public grounds of the city or upon the
premises of another within the city without the consent of the owner of such
premises. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 10, chapter 19 of this code.
6-5-3: OTHER ACTS PROHIBITED:
   (A)   Killing Or Other Mistreatment Of Animals:
      1.   Every person who maliciously kills, maims or wounds an animal, the
property of another; or whoever, having the charge or custody of any animal,
either as owner or otherwise, subjects any animal to needless suffering or
inflicts any unnecessary cruelty upon the same; or, in any manner, abuses an
animal or fails to provide the same with proper food, drink, veterinary care,
shelter or protection from the elements; or who cruelly drives, rides or
otherwise uses the same when unfit for labor, is in violation of this chapter.
      2.   No person shall kill or injure any wild birds within the city;
provided, however, that this section shall not apply to the destruction of
starlings.
      3.   No person shall set a "leg hold type" trapping device to catch an
animal.
   (B)   Interference With Impoundment: No person shall interfere with, hinder,
delay or impede a police officer or animal control officer in the enforcement
of the provisions of this chapter.
   (C)   False Representation: No person shall falsely represent to any police
officer or animal control officer his or her address, nonownership of impounded
animals or other required information.
   (D)   Enticement And Provocation: No person shall wilfully open any door or
gate on any private premises or unleash or coax away any dog or other animal
for the purpose of enticing or enabling any dog or other animal to leave such
premises and be "at large" as defined in section
 6-5-1 of this chapter; neither shall any person tease, torment, or harass a
dog or other animal in such a manner as to cause the animal to emit loud or
disturbing noises or to exhibit dangerous behavior. Such person shall be
strictly liable for violations of this code and/or damages caused by said
animal. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-4: DOG LICENSE REQUIRED; VOLUNTARY LICENSING OF OTHER HOUSEHOLD PETS
PERMITTED:
   (A)   The keeping of any adult dog (over the age of 6 months) or a juvenile
dog (an animal from 2 months of age to 6 months of age) within the city is
hereby forbidden and made an infraction, unless the owner, custodian, keeper or
person harboring the dog shall procure a license from the city for such dog.
Other household pets may be licensed at the option of the owner hereof.
   (B)   License applications, (containing the age, breed, sex, color, rabies
vaccination data, unaltered or neuter status of the animal and name, address
and telephone number of the owner) shall be obtained from the city clerk.
   (C)   Each applicant for a license shall present to the city clerk
satisfactory evidence that every animal over six (6) months of age has been
inoculated against rabies according to standard veterinary practices.
   (D)   Applicants for an altered dog license or for a lifetime dog license
shall be required to swear under penalties of perjury that the animal has in
fact been altered.
   (E)   No late payment penalty shall be charged on new license applications
if the owner has acquired the animal within the preceding thirty (30) days; or
the owner has moved into the city within the preceding thirty (30) days; or the
animal is currently or has been within the preceding thirty (30) days, under
the age which requires a license.
   (F)   All licenses shall expire on December 31 of the year for which they
are issued. A license for the succeeding calendar year can be obtained prior to
the expiration of the current year's license but shall not be effective until
the expiration of the current license. No part of any dog license fee shall be
refundable.
   (G)   Upon payment of the required license fee, the city clerk or designate
shall issue a license to the person applying therefor, which license shall
remain in force until December 31 of that year. The city clerk shall furnish
with such license a metal tag which shall be stamped with a number
corresponding to the number of such license and the year for which it is
issued. Such tag shall be appended to a collar to be worn by the dog at all
times the dog is in view of the public. If a dog tag is lost or destroyed, a
duplicate shall be issued upon proof of payment for the current year and the
payment of one dollar ($1.00) for a replacement tag.
   (H)   This provision shall not apply to an unweaned dog; nor shall it apply
to a nonresident keeping a dog within the city for no longer than sixty (60)
days; nor shall it apply to the keeping of any dog within a properly licensed
kennel or pet shop; nor shall it apply to the keeping of any dog within a
veterinary hospital or animal shelter; nor shall it apply to dogs used in law
enforcement.
   (I)   In any prosecution for violation of this section, the absence of a tag
to be appended to a dog as herein provided, shall be prima facie evidence that
the dog has not been legally licensed.
   (J)   Whenever any person, after applying for and receiving a city dog
license, shall move from the address named in such application, such person
shall, within ten (10) days thereafter, notify the city clerk by telephone or
in writing of such address change. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-5: LICENSES; PROHIBITED ACTS:
   (A)   To remove, steal, mutilate or destroy the license identification tag
of any animal.
   (B)   To refuse to show or exhibit, at any reasonable time, to any animal
control officer or other police officer any dog in his possession or custody,
or to show any license or identification tag issued therefor.
   (C)   To use any license tag for any animal other than the one for which it
was issued.
   (D)   To transfer ownership of a dog without transferring the license
thereto. The person who sold or transferred the pet shall notify the animal
control authority of the name, address, and telephone number of the new owner.
A fee for the transfer of the license is provided for herein. (Ord. 350, 8-8-
2001)
6-5-6: DISPOSITION OF DANGEROUS ANIMALS:
Whenever it shall reasonably appear to an officer, attempting to impound a dog
under the provisions of this chapter, that such dog is dangerous to other
persons and if capture cannot be effected safely and promptly, said officer is
authorized to destroy the dog. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-7: IMPOUNDMENT:
   (A)   In General:
      1.   The animal control officer or any other public safety officer may,
when any animal is found running at large, or is endangering the health, safety
and welfare of the inhabitants of the city, immediately impound the same at the
animal shelter and notify the owner thereof, if known.
      2.   Any officer taking such action or receiving an impounded animal
shall make a registry of such action, entering the breed, color and sex of such
animal and any available license information. If the animal is licensed, an
entry shall be made showing the name and address of the owner and the number of
the license tag.
      3.   If the owner is known or may be determined, the officer may, as an
alternative, or in addition to the impoundment, issue to the owner or custodian
of the animal a citation in the form and manner prescribed by law.
   (B)   Notice Of Impounding:
      1.   Not later than forty eight (48) hours after the impounding of any
animal, the owner or custodian of the animal, if known, shall be notified of
said impoundment. After notice, the owner or custodian of the animal shall have
four (4) days to redeem or file notice of appeal for said animal, describing
the animal and the place and time of taking.
      2.   If the owner or custodian is unknown, written notice of impound
describing said animal shall be posted for not less than five (5) calendar days
at city hall and any other location designated by the city council. Such notice
shall include whether the animal has been declared dangerous.
   (C)   Destruction Of Dangerous Or Diseased Animals:
      1.   Any dangerous animal impounded under the provisions of this article,
or any animal which has bitten any person and is suspected to have rabies or
other disease rendering said animal dangerous to persons, shall be destroyed
and, in the case of suspected rabies, tested according to state health law.
      2.   No animal shall be destroyed during the pendency of any proceeding
to determine whether or not the animal is dangerous.
   (D)   Redemption Of Impounded Animals:
      1.   The owner or custodian of any animal impounded under the provisions
of this chapter may reclaim such dog within six (6) days, or, if the animal is
under quarantine restrictions, ten (10) days, or at the conclusion of any
hearing or court proceeding to determine the dangerous character of the animal
if the conclusion of such hearing is that the animal may be returned to the
owner. Provided that said animal shall be released to the owner or custodian
only upon payment of the dog license fee (including any late fees), if unpaid,
and all impoundment charges, and all charges of maintaining said animal by the
animal shelter (including any veterinary fees incurred).
In no event will an animal under quarantine be released during the quarantine
period without written authorization from the animal control officer.
   (E)   Impound Fees: The owner or other keeper of any animal impounded under
the provisions hereof may recover possession of such animal by payment of the
license fee, if any, and additional sums as follows:
      1.   Daily: Three dollars ($3.00) per day for board and kennel fees.
      2.   Per Offense: For the first three (3) impoundments within a twelve
(12) month period, twenty dollars ($20.00) per impoundment. For any additional
impoundment within any twelve (12) month period, thirty dollars ($30.00).
The fees as stated in this section shall be in addition to whatever penalty may
be imposed as a result of any citation which may be issued for a violation of
this chapter, which penalty is prescribed by section 1-8-1 of this code. Fees
for redemption of livestock are prescribed in section
10-19-4 of this code.
   (F)   Disposition Of Unclaimed Animals: All impounded animals shall be kept
six (6) days, if not sooner redeemed. At the expiration of such time all rights
and interest of the former owner shall terminate and ownership of the animal
shall vest in the city. The animal may be placed in a suitable home or humanely
euthanized.
   (G)   License Required For Release: No unclaimed animal shall be released
from the animal shelter without an appropriate license.
   (H)   Quarantine: Any animal that bites and breaks the skin of any person
shall be quarantined for ten (10) days at the animal shelter or a veterinary
clinic or hospital. If an owner of an animal required to be quarantined under
this section has facilities in which the animal can be securely confined within
an enclosure from which it cannot escape and which is not accessible to the
public, the animal control officer may permit the animal to be quarantined in
such a facility. The owner shall be responsible for all costs of quarantine.
Such animal shall be securely confined within an enclosure from which it cannot
escape and which is not accessible to the public. The animal control officer
shall maintain a record of every animal that bites a person without
provocation. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-8: LICENSE FEES:
License fees are hereby established as follows:
(A) Dog Licenses:
   Annual - unaltered                            $ 10.00
   Annual - altered                              5.00
   Lifetime - available only to altered animals  25.00
   Replacement tag                               1.00
   Transfer fee                                  4.00
   Voluntary registration and licensing of other 4.00
    household pets (each)
(B) Dangerous Dog Registration:
   Annual                                        20.00
(C) Kennels:
   Commercial - annual                           150.00
   Pet shop - annual                             150.00
(D) Late Payment Penalty:
   First 30 days                                 None
   Second 30 days                                10.00
   Thereafter                                    20.00
 
   (E)   Amendments: All fees may be amended by resolution. (Ord. 350, 8-8-
2001)
6-5-9: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
   (A)   The city clerk may, after ten (10) days' written notice, revoke any
license if the person holding the license fails or refuses to comply with any
provision of this chapter.
   (B)   Any person whose dog license is revoked shall, within ten (10) days
thereafter, remove the dog from the city or humanely dispose of the dog, and no
part of the license fee shall be refunded.
   (C)   It shall be condition of the issuance of any dog or kennel license
that any police officer or animal control officer shall be permitted to inspect
all dogs and/or kennels, at any reasonable time, and, if permission for such
inspection is refused, the license shall be revoked.
   (D)   The withholding or falsification of any required information on an
application shall be grounds for refusal to issue a license or for revocation
of a license which has been issued. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-10: PENALTIES:
   (A)   The violation of the following provisions of this chapter shall be a
misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of not to exceed three hundred dollars
($300.00), or imprisonment for a period not to exceed thirty (30) days, or by
both such fine and imprisonment:
      1.   Killing, cruelty or mistreatment of animals 1 .
      2.   Harboring a dangerous animal 2 .
      3.   Interfering with impoundment 3 .
   (B)   Any other violation of this chapter shall be an infraction, punishable
by a fine not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00).
   (C)   Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall
constitute a separate offense.
   (D)   In addition to the fines set forth above, upon a conviction of any
violation under this chapter a court may order an animal forfeited and placed
with the animal shelter for disposition, where the court finds any of the
following circumstances:
      1.   The animal has been cruelly treated, and the cruel treatment is
likely to continue.
      2.   The owner(s) has been convicted of allowing the animal to run at
large on two (2) or more previous occasions, and the animal is likely to
continue to run at large.
      3.   Upon a determination that a dog is dangerous, where the owner(s)
will not or cannot comply with the conditions necessary to keep the animal 4 .
(Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
 
Notes

   6-5-3 of this chapter.

  6-5-2(B) of this chapter.
3 3. See subsection
  6-5-3(B) of this chapter.

  6-5-2(B) of this chapter.
6-5-11: ADDITIONAL REMEDIES:
Any violation of this chapter which continues for more than twenty four (24)
hours is hereby declared to be a public nuisance; and, in addition to any other
civil or criminal remedies, the city may cause such condition to be abated in
the manner provided by law. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-12: LIABILITY OF PARENTS:
In the event that the owner of any animal is a minor, the parent or guardian of
such minor shall be liable for all injuries, property damage, fines and
impoundment fees caused or incurred by such animal. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-13: APPEALS FROM ORDERS OF DESTRUCTION:
   (A)   If the owner of an animal, impounded under an alleged violation of any
regulation of this chapter which could result in the destruction of the animal,
shall believe that there shall not have been a violation thereof, such owner
may appeal the issue to the mayor, praying that the impounded animal not be
destroyed. The impounded animal shall not be destroyed pending resolution of
such owner's appeal.
   (B)   If the owner disagrees with the decision rendered by the mayor, such
owner may petition the magistrate court, praying that the impounded animal not
be destroyed. The impounded animal shall not be destroyed pending resolution of
such owner's appeal.
   (C)   If the court finds that there shall have been a violation and the
animal is destroyed, the owner shall be liable for the cost of impoundment
during the appeal.
   (D)   If the court shall find that there shall not have been a violation,
the animal will be returned to the owner and the city shall be liable for the
cost of impoundment during the appeal.
   (E)   Such matter shall be heard by the court within ten (10) days, or as
soon as the court is able to hear such matter. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-5-14: FEES BY RESOLUTION:
Any fee required by this chapter may be revised by the city council by
resolution. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
CHAPTER 6
FUMIGATING PERMIT REQUIRED
SECTION:
6-6-1: Notice Posted When Fumigating
6-6-2: Permit Required
6-6-3: Penalties
6-6-1: NOTICE POSTED WHEN FUMIGATING:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to fumigate any
dwelling, room, rooms or buildings within the city without first having posted
notices, plainly visible from the outside, on all outside doors of such
dwellings, room, rooms, or buildings. Such notices to give warning that
fumigation is under process within and to give information as to the nature of
the fumigant being used. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-6-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
Before undertaking fumigating as in this chapter described it is hereby
required that a permit be obtained from the city clerk for such fumigating.
(Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-6-3: PENALTIES:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be an infraction,
punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00). (Ord. 350, 8-
8-2001)
CHAPTER 7
ABANDONED CONTAINERS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Abandoned Containers Unlawful
6-7-2: Penalties
6-7-1: ABANDONED CONTAINERS UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure, or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, structure or dwelling under his control, in a place accessible to
children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox, refrigerator or other
container which has a door or lid, snaplock or other locking device which may
not be released from the inside, without first removing said door or lid,
snaplock or other locking device. All such iceboxes, refrigerators or other
containers must have locks removed. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-7-2: PENALTIES:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be an infraction,
punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00). (Ord. 350, 8-
8-2001)
CHAPTER 8
PUBLIC NUISANCES
SECTION:
6-8-1: Public Nuisances Defined
6-8-2: Trash Defined
6-8-3: Junk; Keeping Of Restricted
6-8-4: Penalty
6-8-5: Separate Offense
6-8-6: Civil Penalties
6-8-1: PUBLIC NUISANCES DEFINED:
   (A)   A "public nuisance" is a thing, act, omission, occupation or use of
property which:
      1.   Shall annoy, injure, or endanger the safety, health, comfort or
repose of any considerable number of persons;
      2.   Shall offend the public decency;
      3.   Shall in any way render any considerable number of persons insecure
in life or in use of property.
   (B)   The Genesee city council hereby finds and declares the following
specific acts, omissions, places, conditions and things to be public nuisances:
      1.   Any accumulation of trash, junk, waste, or manure on public or
private property which is not in a proper garbage receptacle;
      2.   Any loud or unusual noises and annoying vibrations which offend the
peace and quiet of two (2) or more persons having ordinary sensibilities;
      3.   All hanging signs, awnings and other similar structures located over
the streets or sidewalks so situated or constructed as to endanger any person;
      4.   Any thing or place whatsoever in which flies, other insects, rats or
rodents are likely to breed or multiply;
      5.   Any accumulation of material or circumstance which may be a fire
danger;
      6.   Any unsightly building, billboard or other structure which is
dangerous, abandoned, or partially destroyed, or any building or structure
commenced and left unfinished (for more than 4 months) or any abandoned well or
excavation not properly protected;
      7.   All places used or maintained as junkyards or dumping grounds or for
the wrecking or disassembling of automobiles, trucks or machinery of any kind,
or for the storing or leaving of worn out, wrecked or abandoned automobiles,
trucks, or machinery of any kind, or of any parts thereof, or the storing or
leaving of any machinery or equipment used by contractors or builders or by
other persons which are not properly zoned or fenced or screened for such use.
Storage of nonoperable vehicles, boats, campers and trailers, equipment and
parts is unlawful unless enclosed in a building or within sight obscuring fence
(fence must be kept in good condition). The storage of materials defined as
"trash" shall not constitute a nuisance if owner maintains a fence which
screens the view of such materials and can demonstrate a reasonable use for
said materials;
      8.   Abandoned, discarded or unused objects or equipment including, but
not limited to, refrigerators, freezers, furniture, stoves, cans, automobile
parts and containers;
      9.   All noxious weeds and unmaintained grass (grass must be kept at 6
inches or less in height);
      10.   Any substance emitting an odor which annoys any person of ordinary
sensibilities;
      11.   Any tree or shrub, whether living or dead, which:
         (a)   Harbors pathogens or injurious insects which reasonably may be
expected to injure or harm other trees or shrubs;
         (b)   Obstructs the free passage of pedestrian or vehicular traffic or
which obstructs a streetlight or traffic control device;
         (c)   By reason of location or condition, constitutes an imminent
danger to the health, safety, or welfare of the general public; or
         (d)   Shall endanger or damage the usefulness of any "street",
"roadway", "sidewalk", "parkway", as those terms are defined in section
9-2-8 of this code, or public sewer or water line, whether growing on private
property or on a parkway;
      12.   Any dead standing or fallen tree or shrub. (Ord. 373, 9-4-2007)
6-8-2: TRASH DEFINED:
"Trash" is defined to include litter, rags, empty barrels, boxes, crates,
packing cases, used tires, used building materials or lumber (not neatly
stacked), used cabinets, used pipe or plumbing fixtures, firewood (not neatly
piled), scrap iron, tin and other metal (not neatly piled). (Ord. 350, 8-8-
2001)
6-8-3: JUNK; KEEPING OF RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or
materials which may be classified as junk adjacent to or in close proximity to
any schoolhouse, church, public parks, public grounds, business buildings or
residences or in a place visible from a public right of way or adjacent
property. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-8-4: PENALTY:
Any person who shall knowingly cause or create any public nuisance, or permit
any public nuisance to be created, or to be placed upon, or to remain upon any
premises owned, used or occupied by him or them, shall be guilty of an
infraction and upon conviction thereof, shall be penalized by a fine not to
exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00), together with costs of such action. The
imposition of one penalty for any violation of this chapter shall not excuse
the violation, or permit it to continue and all such persons shall be required
to correct or remedy such violations, conditions or defects immediately. (Ord.
350, 8-8-2001)
6-8-5: SEPARATE OFFENSE:
Each day's or part of day's continuance of any nuisance set forth in this
chapter shall be a separate offense. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-8-6: CIVIL PENALTIES:
   (A)   The city or any citizen may utilize any civil remedy available by law
to abate said nuisance or obtain a judgment for damages resulting from any of
the nuisances described in this chapter. (Ord. 373, 9-4-2007)
CHAPTER 9
PARADES
SECTION:
6-9-1: Permit Required
6-9-2: Time And Route
6-9-3: Penalties
6-9-1: PERMIT REQUIRED:
Before a parade of any nature is conducted upon the streets of the city a
permit shall be obtained from the city clerk. Traffic or crowd control expenses
will be the responsibility of the applicant and the city clerk may establish a
fee by resolution. (Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-9-2: TIME AND ROUTE:
In order that authorities of the city may take proper steps for the protection
of participants in a parade and to properly control traffic a representative of
the group or organization planning on holding a parade shall at the time of
application for a permit for same give the city clerk information as to the
date of the parade, time of day, nature of the parade and the route planned.
(Ord. 350, 8-8-2001)
6-9-3: PENALTIES:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be an infraction,
punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00). (Ord. 350, 8-
8-2001)
TITLE 7
TRAFFIC
Definitions, General Provisions And Penalties   1
Traffic Control Devices   2
Stopping, Standing And Parking   3
Removal Of Vehicles   4
Bicycles   5
CHAPTER 1
DEFINITIONS, GENERAL PROVISIONS AND PENALTIES
SECTION:
7-1-1: Definitions
7-1-2: Adoption By Reference
7-1-3: Authority Of Police And Fire Department Officials
7-1-4: Speed Limits Designated
7-1-5: Police Department To Investigate Accidents
7-1-6: Abandonment Unlawful
7-1-7: Penalties
7-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
   (A)   Adoption: The city hereby adopts definitions contained in Idaho Code
title 49 for the purposes of enforcement of this title, except as specifically
listed in this section.
   (B)   General Interpretation: Words used in the singular number include the
plural and words used in the plural number include the singular, unless the
context clearly indicates the contrary.
   (C)   Definitions Enumerated: The following listed specified words and terms
are defined as follows:
   ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: An automobile or
personal property which remains upon the streets or other public property for a
continuous period of thirty (30) days, the owner of which cannot be located or
the owner of which refuses to remove the same.
   CHIEF OF POLICE: The individual designated by city council to provide the
duties and obligations described at title 6, chapter 1 of this code. In the
event that no such individual has been designated by city council, the mayor
shall provide such duties and obligations.
   POLICE DEPARTMENT: The public law enforcement agency composed of individuals
employed by the chief of police or the public law enforcement agency contracted
with by city council to provide law enforcement services.
   STOLEN MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: That property which the
police department has reasonable grounds to believe to be stolen.
   UNIDENTIFIED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: As used in this
chapter is hereby defined to be such motor vehicles or other personal property
where ownership thereof cannot be ascertained. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-1-2: ADOPTION BY REFERENCE:
Pursuant to Idaho Code section 49-208(4), the Idaho motor vehicle laws provided
at title 49, Idaho Code are hereby adopted as and for the motor vehicle laws of
the city as though fully set forth herein. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-1-3: AUTHORITY OF POLICE AND FIRE DEPARTMENT OFFICIALS:
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the officers of the police department or such
officers as are assigned by the chief of police to enforce all street traffic
laws of the city and all the state vehicle laws applicable in the city.
   (B)   Officers of the police department or such officers as are assigned by
the chief of police are hereby authorized to direct all traffic by voice, hand
or signal; provided that, in the event of a fire or other emergency or to
expedite traffic or to safeguard pedestrians, officers of the police department
may direct traffic as conditions may require notwithstanding the provisions of
the traffic laws.
   (C)   Officers of the fire department, when at the scene of a fire, may
direct or assist the police in directing traffic through or in the immediate
vicinity. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-1-4: SPEED LIMITS DESIGNATED:
   (A)   Any person driving a vehicle on the streets or highways shall obey any
and all speed limits, as posted by the chief of police. Furthermore, regardless
of the posted speed limit, any person driving a vehicle on the streets or
highways shall drive the same at a careful and prudent speed not greater than
is reasonable and proper, having due regard to traffic, surface and width of
the street or highway and of any other conditions then existing, and no person
shall drive any vehicle upon the street or highway at such a speed as to
endanger the life, limb or property of any person.
   (B)   Unless otherwise posted, or is reasonable and proper, it shall be
unlawful for any person to drive a vehicle at a speed exceeding the following:
      1.   Twelve (12) miles an hour when passing a school during school recess
or while children are going to or leaving school during opening or closing
hours.
      2.   Fifteen (15) miles an hour when approaching within fifty feet (50')
and in traversing an intersection of streets when the driver's view is
obstructed.
      3.   Fifteen (15) miles an hour when approaching within fifty feet (50')
of a grade crossing of any railway when the driver's view is obstructed.
      4.   Twenty (20) miles an hour on all streets in the business district
and twenty five (25) miles an hour on all streets in the residence district,
except under conditions above described. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-1-5: POLICE DEPARTMENT TO INVESTIGATE ACCIDENTS:
It shall be the duty of the police department to investigate traffic accidents,
to arrest and to assist in the prosecution of those persons charged with
violations of law causing or contributing to such accidents. (Ord. 395, 4-16-
2013)
7-1-6: ABANDONMENT UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or any person in charge of a motor vehicle
or other personal property to leave or abandon the same upon the streets or
other public places. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-1-7: PENALTIES:
Any persons violating the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of an
infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished pursuant to this
code and the Idaho Code. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
CHAPTER 2
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES
SECTION:
7-2-1: Authority To Install Traffic Control Devices
7-2-1: AUTHORITY TO INSTALL TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
The chief of police shall place and maintain traffic control signs, signals and
devices when and as required under the traffic regulations of the municipality
to make effective the provisions of said regulations, and may place and
maintain such additional traffic control devices as he may deem necessary.
(Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
CHAPTER 3
STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING
SECTION:
7-3-1: Stop Signs, Yield Signs And Parking Signs
7-3-2: Parking Signs Required
7-3-3: Stopping, Standing Or Parking Prohibited; No Signs Required
7-3-1: STOP SIGNS, YIELD SIGNS AND PARKING SIGNS:
The chief of police may designate through roadways and erect stop signs or
yield signs at specified entrances thereto or may designate any intersection as
a stop intersection or as a yield intersection and erect stop signs or yield
signs at one or more entrances to such intersection. The chief of police may
designate areas within the city as no parking areas and as restricted parking
areas and erect appropriate signs giving notice regarding the extent of the no
parking area and the nature and the extent of the restricted parking area.
(Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-3-2: PARKING SIGNS REQUIRED:
Whenever any parking time limit is imposed or parking is prohibited on
designated streets, it shall be the duty of the chief of police to erect
appropriate signs giving notice thereof and such regulations shall not be
effective unless said signs are erected and in place at the time of any alleged
offense. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-3-3: STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING PROHIBITED; NO SIGNS REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to stop, stand or park a vehicle, except
when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law
or the direction of a law enforcement officer or a traffic control device in
any of the following places:
   (A)   In any place or manner prohibited by title 49, Idaho Code.
   (B)   In any place where signs prohibiting the stopping, standing or parking
of vehicles have been erected at the direction of the chief of police. (Ord.
395, 4-16-2013)
CHAPTER 4
REMOVAL OF VEHICLES
SECTION:
7-4-1: When Police May Remove And Impound A Vehicle; Costs
7-4-2: Enforcement Of Lien On Properties Impounded
7-4-3: Proof Of Ownership; Appeal; Redemption After Sale
7-4-4: Method Of Advertisement And Sale
7-4-1: WHEN POLICE MAY REMOVE AND IMPOUND A VEHICLE; COSTS:
   (A)   The police department may, in its discretion, in addition to the
penalty provided therefor, remove, or cause to be removed, and impound:
      1.   Any vehicle that is parked in a prohibited place, in a prohibited
manner, or at a time when parking is prohibited for a period of ten (10)
minutes or more, when such vehicle is obstructing the free movement of traffic
or is causing a traffic hazard or is directly interfering with the maintenance
or care or emergency use of the streets and the person in charge cannot be
immediately located, or if located, fails, neglects or refuses to move said
vehicle at once.
      2.   Any vehicle that is parked in a time limited area and is in
violation for a period of one hour.
      3.   Any vehicle that is unidentified or wrecked, is a "stolen motor
vehicle or other personal property" as herein defined, or is an "abandoned
motor vehicle or other personal property" as herein defined, found upon any
public street or other property of the city.
      4.   Any vehicle that is parked upon private property without the consent
of the owner of said property, provided the owner of such private property has
first signed a complaint against the owner or operator of said vehicle and
submitted the complaint to the police department.
   (B)   The police department shall store any vehicle it removes and impounds
pursuant to this section in its custody or under its control at such place as
may be designated by the police department until the owner or his authorized
agent applies for same and has paid the costs of removing and storing said
vehicle, which costs shall be assessed and collected by the police department.
The cost of redemption of a removed vehicle shall be the total of the cost of
towing the vehicle to the location of storage and the cost of storage of the
vehicle. Said costs shall be a lien in favor of the city on said vehicle. (Ord.
395, 4-16-2013)
7-4-2: ENFORCEMENT OF LIEN ON PROPERTIES IMPOUNDED:
All motor vehicles and other personal property impounded or heretofore
impounded by the police department and unredeemed by the owner thereof for a
period of sixty (60) days shall thereafter be subject to sale by the chief of
police to the highest bidder for cash as hereinafter provided, and the proceeds
of said sale shall be applied first to all removal and storage charges
accumulated against each article and the remaining balance shall be deposited
with the treasurer and credited with him and shall be kept in a separate fund
for a period of one year from the date of receipt and if at the end of said
year the former owner of said property has not made satisfactory proof of claim
as hereinafter provided then the balance of said proceeds of sale shall be
credited to the general fund of the municipality and the former owner shall
have no further rights to reimbursement. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-4-3: PROOF OF OWNERSHIP; APPEAL; REDEMPTION AFTER SALE:
   (A)   Any person claiming to be the owner of any impounded property shall
make written application therefor to the police department and shall furnish
such additional proof as may be required to establish said ownership. If he
shall present to said department the proof of his ownership of said impounded
property prior to the date of actual sale thereof, then the property itself
shall be delivered to said owner under these conditions; but if said property
has been sold then said department shall endorse its findings of ownership with
a copy of the written application, which application and findings shall be
addressed to the clerk and if presented within one year after said sale, then
such balance of the proceeds of the sale, after deductions, shall be paid to
the owner.
   (B)   Any appeal from the removal, storage and publication costs, if any,
assessed by the police department shall be in the same manner as provided by
law. (Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-4-4: METHOD OF ADVERTISEMENT AND SALE:
Whenever the chief of police shall in his discretion, decide to offer impounded
properties for sale, he shall make a complete and detailed list of said
properties to be included in a publication notice of said sale. The notice of
the sale shall be published by the city clerk at least ten (10) days prior to
the sale of said properties in the official newspaper of the municipality.
(Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
CHAPTER 5
BICYCLES
SECTION:
7-5-1: Obedience To Traffic Control Devices
7-5-2: Speed
7-5-3: Emerging From Alley Or Driveway
7-5-4: Clinging To Vehicles
7-5-5: Carrying Articles
7-5-6: Parking
7-5-7: Riding On Sidewalks
7-5-1: OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
   (A)   Any person operating a bicycle shall obey the instructions of official
traffic control signs, signals and other control devices applicable to vehicles
unless otherwise directed by a police officer.
   (B)   Wherever authorized signs are erected indicating that no right, left
or U-turn is permitted, it shall be unlawful for any person operating a bicycle
to disobey the direction of any such sign, except where a person dismounts from
the bicycle to make such turn in which event such person shall then obey the
regulations applicable to pedestrians. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code; Ord. 395, 4-
16-2013)
7-5-2: SPEED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a bicycle at a speed greater
than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions then existing. (1963 Code;
amd. 1982 Code; Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-5-3: EMERGING FROM ALLEY OR DRIVEWAY:
The operator of a bicycle emerging from an alley, driveway or building shall,
upon approaching a sidewalk or the sidewalk area extending across any alleyway,
yield the right of way to all pedestrians approaching on said sidewalk and upon
entering the roadway shall yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching
on said roadway. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code; Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-5-4: CLINGING TO VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person riding upon any bicycle to attach the same
or himself to any vehicle upon any public thoroughfare. (1963 Code; amd. 1982
Code; Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-5-5: CARRYING ARTICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person operating a bicycle to carry a package,
bundle or article which prevents the rider from keeping at least one hand upon
the handle bars. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code; Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
7-5-6: PARKING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park a bicycle in such a manner as to
interfere or obstruct pedestrian traffic. (1963 Code; amd. 1982 Code; Ord. 395,
4-16-2013)
7-5-7: RIDING ON SIDEWALKS:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle upon a sidewalk
within a business district.
   (B)   The clerk is authorized to erect signs on any sidewalk or roadway
prohibiting the riding of bicycles thereon and when such signs are in place, it
shall be unlawful for any person to disobey the same. (1963 Code; amd. 1982
Code; Ord. 395, 4-16-2013)
TITLE 8
FIRE REGULATIONS
Fire Department   1
Fire Code   2
Fireworks   3
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
8-1-1: Fire Department Established
8-1-2: Personnel; Duties Of Chief
8-1-3: Duties Of Volunteer Members
8-1-4: State Laws To Prevail
8-1-1: FIRE DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established a department herein designated as the city fire
department. (1963 Code)
8-1-2: PERSONNEL; DUTIES OF CHIEF:
The city fire department shall consist of a chief of the fire department, to be
appointed by the mayor and city council, and such other personnel as the mayor
and council may, from time to time, determine necessary.
The duties of the chief of the city fire department shall be as follows:
   (A)   To direct the fighting of fires;
   (B)   To have charge of, be responsible for, and keep in good repair all
equipment and apparatus connected with or belonging to the city fire
department.
   (C)   To call and direct such fire drills and meetings as he deems necessary
for the training of men in efficient firefighting.
   (D)   To have authority over the personnel of the city fire department
during their activities while firefighting and during drills and meetings.
   (E)   To have police authority while on duty as fire chief.
   (F)   To keep records of all fires and make reports of same to each regular
meeting of the city council. (1963 Code)
8-1-3: DUTIES OF VOLUNTEER MEMBERS:
It shall be the duty of volunteer members of the city fire department to
respond to all fire calls, unless prevented from so doing by unavoidable
circumstances. They shall attend fire department drills and meetings and obey
such rules and regulations as are established for the city fire department.
(1963 Code)
8-1-4: STATE LAWS TO PREVAIL:
All public traffic during a fire run and the use and equipment of fire
apparatus shall be governed by state law. (1963 Code)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE CODE
SECTION:
8-2-1: Fire Code Adopted
8-2-2: Definitions
8-2-3: Open Burning Prohibited
8-2-4: Exemptions
8-2-5: Open Burning On Public Property
8-2-6: Penalties
8-2-1: FIRE CODE ADOPTED:
See section
4-1-2 of this Code. (Ord. 402, 7-21-2015, eff. 8-15-2015)
8-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
   LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER: Means any law enforcement duly authorized by the
Mayor and the City Council to act as a law enforcement officer within the
Genesee City limits.
   OPEN BURNING: Means the combustion of any material outside of a building,
house, shop, shed, or other similar structure. (Ord. 411, 7-17-2018)
8-2-3: OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED:
Except as otherwise provided herein, it shall be unlawful to burn garbage,
refuse, weeds, grasses, or any other combustible material within the Genesee
City limits. (Ord. 411, 7-17-2018)
8-2-4: EXEMPTIONS:
The following activities are exempted from the prohibition on open burning:
   (A)   The open burning of leaves, branches and other similar yard debris
from October 1 through May 31 of each year between the hours of eight o'clock
(8:00) A.M. and four o'clock (4:00) P.M., with the following provisions: Open
burning is prohibited during windy days; leaves, branches and yard debris only.
No processed materials. Fires must be a safe distance from all structures. A
pressurized garden hose must be at the fire site.
   (B)   Barbecues, barbecue pits, and fireplaces, provided that all burning
material remains in a non-combustible enclosure and is situated in such manner
that fire cannot spread to any structure, tree, or other item or material.
   (C)   Firefighting training under the direction of the Genesee Fire Chief.
   (D)   Weed or fire hazard control under the direction of the Genesee Fire
Chief.
   (E)   Buildings, structures, and material deemed a hazard to public safety
or health by and under the direction of the Genesee Fire Chief.
   (F)   Any open burn privileges may be revoked by the Mayor, the Genesee Fire
Chief or any law enforcement officer at any time prior to its expiration under
the following circumstances:
      1.   It is deemed that open burning of materials is being done, or will
be done, in a manner that does not comply with the requirements and the
provisions of this chapter.
      2.   It is deemed that the open burning of materials is contrary to the
public health or safety, or is being done in an unsafe or unreasonably
dangerous manner.
      3.   An air quality advisory is issued. (Ord. 411, 7-17-2018)
8-2-5: OPEN BURNING ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
No person shall engage in open burning on any street, public right-of-way,
public easement, alley, or other public property. (Ord. 411, 7-17-2018)
8-2-6: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished by a fine not
to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00), or imprisonment for a period not to
exceed thirty (30) days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 411, 7-
17-2018)
CHAPTER 3
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Enactment Of Regulations
8-3-2: Definitions
8-3-3: Dangerous Fireworks; Public Display
8-3-4: Safe And Sane Fireworks
8-3-5: Applications For Permits
8-3-6: Investigation Of Applicant
8-3-7: Grant Or Deny Permit
8-3-8: Term Of Permit; Filing
8-3-9: Liability Insurance
8-3-10: Hours Of Sale
8-3-11: Fireworks Stands; Regulation Of Sales
8-3-12: Evidence Of Source Of Fireworks
8-3-13: Removal Of Stands; Bond Or Deposit
8-3-14: Compliance With State Law
8-3-15: Violation
8-3-1: ENACTMENT OF REGULATIONS:
The city council does hereby enact regulations for the sale and discharge of
fireworks in the city as set forth in this chapter. (1982 Code)
8-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
   DANGEROUS FIREWORKS: Shall include any of the following:
   (A)   Firecrackers, cannon crackers, giant crackers, salutes, silver tube
salutes, cherry bombs, mines, ground bombardment, grasshoppers and other
explosive articles of similar nature;
   (B)   Blank cartridges;
   (C)   Skyrockets and rockets, including similar devices employing any
combustible or explosive material and which rise in the air during discharge,
except model rockets and model rocket engines designed, sold and used for the
purpose of repelling of recoverable aero model rockets;
   (D)   Roman candles, including all devices which discharge balls of fire
into the air;
   (E)   Chasers and whistles, including all devices which dart or travel about
the surface of the ground during the discharge;
   (F)   Snakes and hats containing bichloride of mercury;
   (G)   Sparklers more than ten inches (10") in length or one-quarter inch (1/
4") in diameter;
   (H)   All articles for pyrotechnic display such as aerial shells, salutes,
flash shells, sky battles, parachute shells, mines, dago bombs and similar
devices;
   (I)   All torpedoes which explode by means of friction or which contain
arsenic and all other similar fireworks devices including cracker balls;
   (J)   Fire balloons or balloons of any type which have burning material of
any kind attached thereto.
   FIREWORKS: Blank cartridges, toy pistols, toy cannons, toy canes or toy guns
in which explosives are used, fire balloons (balloons of a type which have
burning material of any kind attached thereto or which require fire underneath
to propel them), firecrackers, torpedoes, skyrockets, rockets, Roman candles,
fountain wheels, dago bombs, sparklers and other fireworks of like construction
and any fireworks containing any combustible or explosive substance for the
purpose of producing a visible or audible effect by combustion, deflagration,
explosion or detonation.
Exempted from this definition are all toy pistols, toy cannons, toy canes and
toy guns and similar devices such as party poppers or party favors in which
paper caps containing not more than twenty five hundredths (0.25) grain of
explosive compound per cap are used and such caps whether single, roll or tape
type.
   SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS: Shall include any of the following:
   (A)   Cone fountains with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding fifty grams
(50 g) each;
   (B)   Cylindrical fountains, whether base, spike or handle, with pyrotechnic
composition not exceeding seventy five grams (75 g) each and inside tube
diameter not exceeding three-quarters inch (3/4");
   (C)   Sparklers and "dipped sticks" not more than ten inches (10") in length
or one-quarter inch (1/4") in diameter and Suzuki and morning glories with
pyrotechnic composition not exceeding four grams (4 g) each;
   (D)   Snakes which do not contain bichloride of mercury and pyrotechnic
composition not exceeding two grams (2 g) each;
   (E)   Wheels with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding sixty (60) grains
for each driver unit or two hundred forty (240) grains for each complete wheel.
The inside tube diameter of driver unit shall not exceed one-half inch (1/2");
   (F)   Whistles, without report and which do not dart or travel about the
ground during discharge with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding six grams (6
g) and containing no picric or gallic acid. (1982 Code)
8-3-3: DANGEROUS FIREWORKS; PUBLIC DISPLAY:
   (A)   Permit Required: It shall be unlawful for any person in the city to
import, export, offer for sale, sell, possess, keep or store or permit the
keeping or storing of any "dangerous fireworks" for any use or purpose, except
that a person holding a "dangerous fireworks permit" issued pursuant to the
terms and conditions of this chapter may use "dangerous fireworks" for a safely
supervised and conducted public display of fireworks and said fireworks may be
stored for a period of not exceeding four (4) days immediately preceding the
date of said public display; provided the fireworks are to be used exclusively
for the public display.
   (B)   Application; Fee: Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or
furtherance of any legitimate personal, business or charitable purpose,
desiring to make a public display of "dangerous fireworks" shall first make
written application to the city clerk for a "dangerous fireworks permit". Each
applicant shall pay to the city clerk a fee of five dollars ($5.00) at the time
he files his application. At the time and as a condition of such filing, and
with each application, each applicant shall pay an additional fee to defray
costs of preliminary investigations required hereunder, and to be conducted by
the fire chief, which fee shall be five dollars ($5.00) per site applied for,
and shall not be refundable in any event. (1982 Code)
8-3-4: SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS:
   (A)   Permit Required: No person, without having a valid "safe and sane
fireworks permit" issued pursuant to terms and conditions set forth in this
code shall import, export, possess for the purpose of sale, offer for sale,
give away, or sell any "safe and sane fireworks" for any use or purpose.
   (B)   Application; Fee: Any reputable person in reasonable pursuit or
furtherance of any legitimate personal, business or charitable purpose,
desiring to engage in the sale of "safe and sane fireworks" within the city
shall first make written application to the city clerk for a "safe and sane
fireworks permit". Each applicant shall pay to the city clerk a fee of five
dollars ($5.00) at the time he files his application. In the event no "safe and
sane fireworks permit" is issued by the city council by June 15 in the year
during which the application is made, the city clerk shall refund the
application fee. At the time and as a condition of such filing, and with each
application, each applicant shall pay an additional fee to defray costs of
preliminary investigations required hereunder and to be conducted by the fire
chief, which fee shall be five dollars ($5.00) per site applied for, and shall
not be refundable in any event. (1982 Code)
8-3-5: APPLICATIONS FOR PERMITS:
Each applicant for a "safe and sane fireworks permit" or a "dangerous fireworks
permit" shall file his application with the city clerk. Each application shall
show the following:
   (A)   Name and address of applicant.
   (B)   The purpose for which the applicant is primarily existing and for
which it is organized.
   (C)   The names and addresses of the officers, trustees or directors, if
any, of the applicant.
   (D)   The location where the applicant requests permission to sell "safe and
sane fireworks" or display "dangerous fireworks".
   (E)   When and where the applicant was organized and established, or, if a
natural person, the applicant's age.
   (F)   The location of the applicant's principal and permanent meeting place
or places, or principal place or places of business.
   (G)   The applicant's state sales tax permit number.
   (H)   If the applicant is an entity other than a sole proprietorship, the
name and a general description of the business activities of each parent or
subsidiary company, business or entity, and a general description of the
ownership organization of each parent or subsidiary, if any.
   (I)   Such other information as the city clerk may require on a standard
form submitted to all applicants and which is reasonably necessary to protect
the public health, safety and morals. (1982 Code)
8-3-6: INVESTIGATION OF APPLICANT:
The city clerk shall cause an investigation to be made of each application and
applicant and shall submit a written report of his findings and recommendations
for or against the issuance of the permit, together with his reasons therefor,
to the city council, which report shall not be public information except on
request of the applicant or by order of the city council. (1982 Code)
8-3-7: GRANT OR DENY PERMIT:
The city council shall have the power in its discretion to grant or deny any
application, subject to such reasonable conditions, if any, as it shall
prescribe so long as the denial of the application or any conditions imposed on
the granting of the application are reasonably necessary for protection of the
public health, safety and morals. (1982 Code)
8-3-8: TERM OF PERMIT; FILING:
A "safe and sane fireworks permit" or a "dangerous fireworks permit" issued
pursuant to this chapter shall be valid only within the calendar year in which
issued. A permit shall be valid only for the specific premises or location
designated in the permit. However, subject to reasonable conditions necessary
for protection of the public health, safety and morals, an applicant may be
granted permits for more than one site or location within the city. No permit
shall be transferable or assignable.
Each application for a permit to sell "safe and sane fireworks" at retail shall
be filed with the city clerk on or before May 30 of the calendar year for which
the permit is sought. (1982 Code)
8-3-9: LIABILITY INSURANCE:
Each applicant for a "safe and sane fireworks permit" or for a "dangerous
fireworks permit" shall have filed with the city clerk prior to the issuance
and validity of any permit, a policy, or a certified true copy thereof, of
public liability and products liability insurance, including both "accident"
and "occurrence" coverage. The insurance coverage limits for both public
liability coverage and for products liability coverage shall be at least one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per person per occurrence bodily injury,
three hundred thousand dollars ($300,000.00) per occurrence aggregate bodily
injury and one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per occurrence aggregate
property damage. Each policy shall be in form and substance acceptable to the
city council, and shall name as insured parties under the terms of the policy
the city, all officials of the city in the performance of official functions
regarding all operations under or pertaining to said permit, any licensee or
licensor of the applicant, and all vendors of the fireworks covered by the
permit to be issued to the applicant. Said policy of insurance shall be so
written that it cannot be canceled without at least ten (10) days' prior
written notice to the city from the underwriting insurance company. The policy
of insurance shall be underwritten through or by a qualified and duly licensed
insurance company or companies doing or authorized to do insurance business in
Idaho. (1982 Code)
8-3-10: HOURS OF SALE:
No "safe and sane fireworks" shall be given away, sold or offered for sale,
except from twelve o'clock (12:00) noon on June 15 to twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight on July 5 of each year. (1982 Code)
8-3-11: FIREWORKS STANDS; REGULATION OF SALES:
   (A)   Temporary fireworks stands from which "safe and sane fireworks" are to
be sold shall be subject to the following provisions:
      1.   The stand in which the fireworks will be stored or sold shall not be
located within twenty five feet (25') of any other building nor within one
hundred feet (100') of any gasoline station or flammable liquid dispensing
device or installation.
      2.   All such stands shall meet the structural stability requirements of
the building regulations of the city and all lighting circuits and other
electrical equipment shall meet the requirements of the electrical regulations
of the city.
      3.   The stand shall have exit doors at least thirty inches (30") wide at
both ends of the structure and one additional door for each twenty five feet
(25') of rear wall in excess of twenty five feet (25'). All doors shall open
outward from the stand and all doorways shall be kept free and clear from all
supplies and materials at all times.
      4.   Each stand shall be provided with a minimum of two (2) 21/2-gallon
"soda and acid" type fire extinguishers, in good working order, and easily
accessible for use in case of fire, which shall be kept in immediate proximity
to the location where the fireworks are retailed.
      5.   There shall be at least one supervisor, twenty one (21) years of age
or older on duty at all times. All fireworks shall be effectively kept away
from any kind of self-service by the public, and shall be placed in a location
which is unavailable and inaccessible to members of the public in capacities
other than as legal customers.
No person under sixteen (16) years of age shall be allowed inside the temporary
stand at any time, nor shall any person under sixteen (16) years of age work at
or about any stand where safe and sane fireworks are sold or offered for sale.
      6.   No person employed as a watchman shall be permitted to remain inside
any stand when it is not open for business.
      7.   "No Smoking" signs shall be prominently displayed both inside and
outside the stand. No smoking shall be permitted within the stand or within
fifteen feet (15') of the stand.
      8.   No temporary stand shall be erected before June 10 of any year. The
premises on which the stand is erected shall be cleared of all structures and
debris, not later than twelve o'clock (12:00) noon of July 7.
      9.   No fireworks shall be discharged in or within twenty five feet (25')
of any fireworks stand.
      10.   No person shall allow any rubbish to accumulate in or around any
fireworks stand or permit a fire nuisance to exist.
      11.   No fireworks shall remain unattended at any time regardless of
whether the fireworks stand is open for business or not. If any fireworks are
stored, they shall only be stored at such places as are approved for storage of
fireworks by the fire chief.
      12.   No stand shall have a floor area in excess of seven hundred fifty
(750) square feet.
   (B)   Permanent business structures from which "safe and sane fireworks" are
to be sold shall be subject to the following provisions:
      1.   All such buildings shall meet the structural stability requirements
of the building regulations of the city and all lighting circuits and other
electrical equipment shall meet the requirements of the electrical regulations
of the city.
      2.   The building shall have exit doors at least thirty inches (30") wide
at both ends of the structure and shall otherwise conform to the exit
regulations established by the city building regulations for structures of the
size and nature of said building. All doorways shall be kept free and clear
from all supplies and materials at all times.
      3.   Each building shall be provided with such number of fire
extinguishers as the fire chief of the city shall deem adequate, but in all
cases the number shall be not less than two (2). The fire extinguishers shall
be two and one-half (21/2) gallon "soda and acid" type extinguishers or other
types approved by the fire chief. The fire extinguishers shall be in good
working order, easily accessible for use in case of fire and kept in immediate
proximity to the location where the fireworks are retailed.
      4.   There shall be at least one supervisor, twenty one (21) years of age
or older on duty at all times. No person under sixteen (16) years of age shall
be allowed at any time to sell such fireworks.
      5.   "No Smoking" signs shall be prominently displayed in the immediate
area. No smoking shall be permitted within fifteen feet (15') of such area
where fireworks are displayed.
      6.   No fireworks shall be discharged in or within twenty five feet (25')
of the area where fireworks are kept.
      7.   No person shall allow any rubbish to accumulate, or permit a fire
nuisance to exist in or around the area where fireworks are sold.
      8.   If fireworks are stored, they shall only be stored in such places as
are approved for storage of fireworks by the fire chief.
      9.   No building where alcoholic beverages are sold for consumption on
the premises shall be used for the retail sale of "safe and sane fireworks".
      10.   The city council may establish other regulations for permanent
structures where fireworks are to be sold so long as said regulations are
reasonably necessary to protect the public health, safety and morals, and apply
uniformly to all applicants. (1982 Code)
8-3-12: EVIDENCE OF SOURCE OF FIREWORKS:
Each permittee shall be required to retain at the licensed premises while said
premises are open, and at his principal place of business for a year
thereafter, copies of all invoices, receipts and orders evidencing the source
from which he acquired the fireworks which he handled. (1982 Code)
8-3-13: REMOVAL OF STANDS; BOND OR DEPOSIT:
In those cases where the applicant conducts the sale of fireworks from a
temporary fireworks stand, he shall post with the city clerk a cash bond or
cash deposit in the amount of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) (or such
other security as may be acceptable to the city clerk) conditioned upon the
prompt removal of the temporary fireworks stand and the cleaning up of debris
from the site of the temporary fireworks stand, which deposit or security shall
be returned to the applicant only in the event he removes said temporary
fireworks stand and cleans up all debris to the satisfaction of the city
council, or such other official as the city council may designate. In the event
of the applicant's failure to so remove the stand and debris, said cash bond or
cash deposit shall be forfeited to the city. In no event shall the applicant be
entitled to the return of said cash bond or cash deposit if he has failed to
remove said temporary fireworks stand and clean up all debris by twelve o'clock
(12:00) noon of July 7 of any year. It shall be the legal duty of each
permittee to clear such sites and remove all debris therefrom on or before July
6 of the year in which the permit is granted, and failure to do so shall be
punishable as hereinafter provided. (1982 Code)
8-3-14: COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW:
It shall be the duty of every person issued a "fireworks permit" to comply with
all the provisions of the Idaho state fireworks act 1  and this chapter. The
conviction of violation of the aforesaid Idaho state fireworks act or any of
the provisions of this chapter by the permittee, or by any of its agents,
employees or officers shall constitute a cause, in and of itself, to deny any
subsequent application for a permit. (1982 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 39-2605 et seq.
8-3-15: VIOLATION:
Any person who violates this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof shall be punished accordingly. (1982 Code)
TITLE 9
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
Removal Of Snow And Ice   1
Trees And Shrubbery   2
Sidewalks And Curbs   3
Weed Control   4
Public Right Of Way Construction, Excavation And Repair   5
CHAPTER 1
REMOVAL OF SNOW AND ICE
SECTION:
9-1-1: Remove Snow And Ice
9-1-2: Notice To Be Given
9-1-3: Upon Failure To Comply, City To Remove
9-1-1: REMOVE SNOW AND ICE:
It shall be the duty of any owner, tenant or occupant of any premises abutting
or adjoining any public sidewalk to remove all snow and ice from any such
sidewalk. (1963 Code)
9-1-2: NOTICE TO BE GIVEN:
Failure of any owner, occupant or tenant to remove snow and ice from public
sidewalks, as specified in section
9-1-1 of this chapter, within a period of four (4) hours shall be deemed a
violation of the provisions of this chapter. (1963 Code)
9-1-3: UPON FAILURE TO COMPLY, CITY TO REMOVE:
Upon failure of the owner, tenant or occupant of said premises to comply with
the provisions of this chapter, then the city shall have the right to remove
such snow and ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the
sidewalks. Such assessment to be certified to the county assessor or other
proper county official having charge of the making of the assessment roll, and
such assessment to be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the same
manner as other municipal taxes are collected. (1963 Code)
CHAPTER 2
TREES AND SHRUBBERY
SECTION:
9-2-1: Policy Statement
9-2-2: City Tree Administrator
9-2-3: Shade Tree Commission
9-2-4: Organization And Meetings
9-2-5: Duties Of Commission
9-2-6: Authority And Control Over Trees
9-2-7: Permit Required; Application
9-2-8: Definitions
9-2-9: Trimming Trees
9-2-10: Unlawful To Abuse Trees
9-2-11: Hedges And Shrubbery
9-2-1: POLICY STATEMENT:
The city hereby declares that it shall be the policy of the city to protect
trees planted and growing within the public rights of way, city parks, the city
cemetery and within or on all other property owned or otherwise under the
control of the city. (Ord. 312, 4-6-1992)
9-2-2: CITY TREE ADMINISTRATOR:
The office of city tree administrator is hereby established. The city tree
administrator may be a member of the city council or an appointed official or
an employee of the city, appointed to the office of city tree administrator by
the mayor and confirmed by the city council. The city tree administrator shall
administer the provisions of this chapter and shall have all administrative
powers in connection therewith which are not specifically assigned to some
other person or body. The city tree administrator shall have the following
authority and duties:
   (A)   Supervise in planting, pruning, spraying, preserving and removal of
