less than one square inch for every square foot of enclosed area subject to
flooding shall be provided.
            (2)   The bottom of all openings shall be no higher than one foot
(1') above grade.
            (3)   Openings may be equipped with screens, louvers or other
coverings or devices; provided that they permit the automatic entry and exit of
floodwaters.
      2.   Nonresidential Construction: New construction and substantial
improvement of any commercial, industrial or other nonresidential structure
shall either have the lowest floor, including basement, elevated to the level
of the base flood elevation or together with attendant utility and sanitary
facilities, shall:
         (a)   Be floodproofed so that below the base flood level the structure
is watertight with walls substantially impermeable to the passage of water;
         (b)   Have structural components capable of resisting hydrostatic and
hydrodynamic loads and effects of buoyancy;
         (c)   Be certified by a registered professional engineer or architect
that the design and methods of construction are in accordance with accepted
standards of practice for meeting provisions of this subsection based on their
development and/or review of the structural design, specifications and plans.
Such certifications shall be provided to the official as set forth in
subsection
10-13-4(D)3(b) of this chapter;
         (d)   Nonresidential structures that are elevated, not floodproofed,
must meet the same standards for space below the lowest floor as described in
subsection (F)1(b) of this section.
         (e)   Applicants floodproofing nonresidential buildings shall be
notified that flood insurance premiums will be based on rates that are one foot
(1') below the floodproofed level (e.g., a building constructed to the base
flood level will be rated as 1 foot below that level).
      3.   Manufactured Homes: All manufactured homes to be placed or
substantially improved within zones A1-30, AH, and AE shall be elevated on a
permanent foundation such that the lowest floor of the manufactured home is at
one foot (1') above the base flood elevation and be securely anchored to an
adequately anchored foundation system in accordance with the provisions of
subsection (A)2 of this section.
   (G)   Floodways: Located within areas of special flood hazard established in
subsection
10-13-3(B) of this chapter are areas designed as floodways. Since the floodway
is an extremely hazardous area due to the velocity of floodwaters which carry
debris, potential projectiles and erosion potential, the following provisions
apply:
      1.   Prohibit encroachments, including fill, new construction,
substantial improvements and other development unless certification by a
registered professional engineer or architect is provided demonstrating that
encroachments shall not result in any increase in flood levels during the
occurrence of the base flood discharge.
      2.   If subsection (G)1 of this section is satisfied, all new
construction and substantial improvements shall comply with all applicable
flood hazard reduction provisions of this section. (Ord. 292, 3-16-1987)
 
Notes
1 1. Reference FEMA's manufactured home installation in flood hazard areas
  guidebook for additional techniques.
2 1. See subsection
  10-13-4(D)2 of this chapter.
CHAPTER 14
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
10-14-1: Administrative Standards
10-14-2: Zoning Administrator
10-14-3: Penalty
10-14-4: Complaints
10-14-5: Variances
10-14-6: Schedule Of Fees
10-14-1: ADMINISTRATIVE STANDARDS:
Whenever, in the course of administration and enforcement of the provisions in
this title, it is necessary or desirable to make any administrative decision,
then, unless other standards in this title are provided, the decision shall be
made so that the result will not be contrary to the spirit and purpose of this
title or injurious to the surrounding neighborhood. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
10-14-2: ZONING ADMINISTRATOR:
The office of the zoning administrator is hereby established. The administrator
shall be appointed by the council. The administrator may also serve in some
other capacity as an employee or appointed officer of the city of Genesee. He
shall administer the provisions of this title and shall have all administrative
powers in connection therewith which are not specifically assigned to some
other officer or body. He shall have no power to vary or waive ordinance
requirements.
   (A)   Zoning Permit: No building or structure shall be erected, added to or
structurally altered unless a zoning permit has been issued by the
administrator or his authorized representative. Any person desiring to obtain
such a permit shall file with the administrator a zoning permit application
describing fully the premises whereon such work is proposed and setting out in
detail the location of all such proposed work on the premises. The fee for a
zoning permit shall be as specified under the schedule of fees adopted by the
city.
   (B)   Zoning Permit For Manufactured Homes: No manufactured home shall be
assembled, erected, added to or structurally changed unless a zoning permit has
been issued by the administrator or his authorized representative to ensure
that the manufactured home is assembled to standards regulating the anchoring
of the structure to its foundation and other building requirements that meet or
exceed the standards of the uniform building code. Any person desiring to
obtain such a permit shall submit a zoning permit application on a prescribed
form which shall include, in addition to such information as is generally
required for zoning permits and is necessary for administrative purposes, all
information necessary to determine the manufactured home's conformity with
chapter 20 of this title, including exterior dimensions, roofing pitch, roofing
material, size of overhangs, exterior siding material, foundations fascia and
other applicable information. The zoning permit application shall be signed by
the applicant and the applicant shall provide all information necessary to
verify such structure does meet the definition of manufactured home and does
meet the standards of chapter 20 of this title, prior to moving said structure
to the building site. The administrator or his authorized representative,
following the issuance of the zoning permit and upon inspection of the site for
the attachment of the structure to a foundation base, shall verify in writing
that all standards of chapter 20 of this title have been met as certified by
the applicant in the application form.
   (C)   Responsibility Of Applicant: It shall be the responsibility of the
applicant to locate and establish all property lines to the reasonable
satisfaction of the administrator. The administrator may obtain the advice of
the council regarding the location and establishment of property lines and may
require a survey of the premises.
   (D)   Inspection: The administrator and his authorized representative are
hereby empowered to cause any building, other structure or tract of land to be
inspected and examined and to order in writing the remedying of any condition
found to exist therein or thereat in violation of any provisions of this title.
After any such order has been served no work shall proceed on any building,
other structure or tract of land covered by such order, except to correct or
comply with such violation.
   (E)   Injunction: In addition to any of the foregoing remedies the city
attorney, acting in behalf of the council, may maintain any action for the
injunction to restrain; any violation of this title. (Ord. 281, 11-4-1985)
10-14-3: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this title, upon
conviction thereof, shall be fined not more than three hundred dollars
($300.00) or imprisoned not more than one hundred eighty (180) days, or both.
Each day during which the illegal erection, construction, reconstruction,
alteration, maintenance or use continues shall be deemed a separate offense.
(Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
10-14-4: COMPLAINTS:
Any person aggrieved by a violation of the provisions of this title may file a
written complaint with the administrator, who shall immediately investigate
such complaint and take action to have the violation removed, if such a
violation is, in fact, found to exist. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
10-14-5: VARIANCES:
   (A)   Power To Grant Variances: The commission may grant a variance only if
all the following requirements, insofar as applicable, have been satisfied:
      1.   There are unique physical circumstances or conditions such as
irregularity, narrowness or shallowness of the lot or exceptional topographical
or other physical conditions peculiar to the property;
      2.   The unusual circumstances or conditions do not exist throughout the
neighborhood or district in which the property is located;
      3.   Because of such physical circumstances or conditions, the property
cannot reasonably be developed in conformity with the provisions of this zoning
title;
      4.   Such unnecessary hardship has not been created by the applicant;
      5.   The variance, if granted, will not alter the essential character of
the neighborhood or district in which the property is located nor substantially
or permanently impair the appropriate use or development of adjacent property;
      6.   The variance, if granted, is the minimum variance that will afford
relief and is the least modification possible of the zoning ordinance
provisions which are in question.
   (B)   Hearing Procedure For Variances: Upon receipt of the application for a
variance the commission shall follow the notice and hearing procedures provided
in subsection
10-8-6(B) of this title. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
10-14-6: SCHEDULE OF FEES:
   (A)   The council shall establish a schedule of fees for zoning permits,
appeals, amendments and other matters pertaining to the provisions of this
title. The schedule of fees may be altered or amended only by the council.
(Ord. 230, 6-21-1976; amd. Ord. 267, 5-4-1981)
   (B)   Until all applicable fees, charges and expenses have been paid in full
no action shall be taken on any application or appeal. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
CHAPTER 15
BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT
SECTION:
10-15-1: Organization Of Board Of Adjustment
10-15-2: Powers Of The Board
10-15-3: Appeal Procedure
10-15-1: ORGANIZATION OF BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT:
   (A)   There is hereby created a board of adjustment (hereinafter called the
board) to aid in the administration of the provisions of this title. The
council is responsible for appointing the membership of the board. In the event
no board is appointed the council shall perform the duties and functions of the
board.
   (B)   The board shall elect a chairman and adopt such rules of procedure
which may be necessary or convenient for carrying out its function. All
meetings shall be open to the public and records shall be kept of all requests
and actions taken. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
10-15-2: POWERS OF THE BOARD:
The board shall hear and decide appeals from any decision or requirement made
by the administrator. Every decision made by the board shall be based upon
findings of fact and must be supported in the records of the board. (Ord. 267,
5-4-1981)
10-15-3: APPEAL PROCEDURE:
Any person denied a zoning permit under this title shall have the right to
appeal within fifteen (15) days after being notified of the action of the
administrator.
The notice of appeal must be in writing and filed with the administrator and
must be accompanied by a fee adopted by the city. The notice of appeal shall
state specifically the basis of the appeal. As soon as practicable after
receiving the notice of appeal, the board shall fix a date, time and place for
hearing the appeal by the board. Written notice of the time and place of the
hearing shall be given at least fifteen (15) days prior to the date of the
hearing to each appellant. The board must render a decision within thirty (30)
days of the date of the hearing.
Only those matters or issues specified by the notice of appeal shall be
considered in the hearing of the appeal. (Ord. 267, 5-4-1981)
CHAPTER 16
REZONING POLICY AND STANDARDS; CONFLICTS
SECTION:
10-16-1: Declaration Of Policy And Standards For Rezoning
10-16-2: Conflict With Other Laws
10-16-1: DECLARATION OF POLICY AND STANDARDS FOR REZONING:
For the purpose of establishing and maintaining sound, stable and desirable
development within the city of Genesee the rezoning of land is to be
discouraged and allowed only under certain circumstances as provided hereafter.
The zoning map is the result of a detailed and comprehensive appraisal of the
city's present and future needs regarding land use allocation and, as such,
should not be amended unless to correct a manifest error or because of changed
or changing conditions in a particular area or the city in general. Rezonings
shall only be allowed if the applicant demonstrates by clear and convincing
evidence that:
   (A)   The land to be rezoned was zoned in error and as presently zoned is
inconsistent with the policies and goals of the city's comprehensive plan; or
   (B)   The area for which rezoning is requested has changed or is changing to
such a degree that it is in the public interest to encourage a redevelopment of
the area; or
   (C)   The proposed rezoning is necessary in order to provide land for a
community related use which was not anticipated at the time of the adoption of
the city's comprehensive plan, and that such rezoning will be consistent with
the policies and goals of the comprehensive plan.
This declaration of standards for rezoning shall not control a rezoning which
occurs incidental to a comprehensive revision of the city's zoning map. (Ord.
230, 6-21-1976)
10-16-2: CONFLICT WITH OTHER LAWS:
   (A)   Whenever regulations or restrictions imposed by the provisions of this
title are in conflict with the regulations or restrictions imposed by any
governmental authority through legislation, rules, regulations, restrictions,
ordinances or resolutions, the more restrictive or those which impose higher
standards or requirements shall govern.
   (B)   Regardless of any other provisions of this title, no land shall be
used and no structure erected or maintained in violation of any state or
federal pollution control or environmental protection law or regulation. (Ord.
230, 6-21-1976)
CHAPTER 17
ANNEXATIONS
SECTION:
10-17-1: Annexed Territory
10-17-1: ANNEXED TERRITORY:
   (A)   Prior to annexation of an unincorporated area, the council shall
request and receive a recommendation from the commission on the proposed plan
and zoning ordinance changes for the unincorporated area. The commission and
the council shall follow the notice and hearing procedures provided in section
10-12-4 of this title.
   (B)   Concurrently or immediately following the adoption of an ordinance of
annexation, the council shall amend the comprehensive plan and zoning ordinance
if applicable. (Ord. 230, 6-21-1976)
CHAPTER 18
CITY IMPACT AREA
ARTICLE A. LATAH COUNTY AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
10-18A-1: Area
10-18A-2: Definitions
10-18A-3: Governing Plan And Ordinances
10-18A-4: Administration Of The Area Of City Impact
10-18A-5: Appeals
10-18A-6: Enforcement
10-18A-7: Renegotiation
10-18A-8: Agreement With Latah County
10-18A-1: AREA:
The Genesee area of city impact agreement shall affect the unincorporated area
of Latah County within the following sections: 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, Township
37 North, Range 05 West, B.M., as depicted on the map attached to the ordinance
codified herein, and as provided in the revised Genesee area of city impact and
agreement and in Latah County ordinance 307. Land outside the city limits, but
within the above described area shall be deemed within the Genesee area of city
impact. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words when used herein shall have these meanings:
   ADMINISTRATIVE REQUESTS: Applications, requests, determinations, or
interpretations other than quasi-judicial and "legislative actions" as defined
herein, such as land divisions, zoning determinations, floodplain
determinations, zoning interpretations of the zoning administrator or designee,
and other administrative actions.
   AREA: The city of Genesee's area of city impact.
   BOARD: The board of Latah County commissioners.
   CITY: The city of Genesee.
   COMPLAINTS: Written requests for enforcement under the ordinances adopted
pursuant to section
10-18A-3 of this article.
   COUNTY: Latah County.
   LEGISLATIVE ACTIONS: Amendments to the zoning map or ordinances, and other
similar decisions by a governing board sitting in a legislative capacity, where
its decision produces a general rule or policy applicable to an open class of
individuals, interests, or situations.
   QUASI-JUDICIAL APPLICATIONS: Applications for decisions or determinations
regarding property located within the area, which are made by a governing board
or its designee sitting in a quasi- judicial capacity, where its decision
involves the application of a general rule or policy to specific individuals,
interests, or situations, including, but not limited to, conditional use
permits, special use permits, planned unit developments, subdivisions,
variances, rezones, and other quasi-judicial proceedings. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-3: GOVERNING PLAN AND ORDINANCES:
   (A)   The county's comprehensive plan (resolution 2010-32), land use
ordinance (ordinance 269, as amended), and fee schedule (resolution 2002-15),
and subsequent amendments thereto, are hereby adopted by the county for the
area. All other applicable county ordinances and resolutions are still in
effect for the area.
   (B)   The county will adopt or has adopted this agreement in Latah County
ordinance 307.
   (C)   This agreement supersedes and replaces the prior Genesee area of city
impact agreement between the parties hereto which was approved by the parties
on January 31, 2000.
   (D)   No amendments of the plan or zoning and subdivision ordinances in the
area shall be effective until adopted by the city as required by its ordinances
and thereafter by the county. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-4: ADMINISTRATION OF THE AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
   (A)   Administration: The county shall administer the applicable ordinances
and resolutions for the area, as identified in subsection
10-18A-3(A) of this article.
   (B)   Applications, Permits Made To County: All applications, requests for
permits, and inquiries regarding property located within the area, which are
made pursuant to the ordinances adopted under section
10-18A-3 of this article, shall be made to the county. The county shall charge
and collect a fee based upon the adopted county fee schedule, as identified in
subsection
10-18A-3(A) of this article.
   (C)   County To Notify City: The county shall process administrative
requests in the area without input from the city, however, the county will
notify the city of administrative requests, such as building permits or land
divisions, within ten (10) days of receipt of such request. The city and county
recognize that some administrative requests, such as zoning interpretations or
buildable parcel determinations, are informal and can be addressed by county
staff without the need to notify the city.
   (D)   Quasi-Judicial Applications:
      1.   Quasi-judicial applications shall be reviewed by the county staff
and scheduled for the required public hearing(s) before the Latah County zoning
commission and/or the board of county commissioners, as specified by the Latah
County land use ordinance.
      2.   The county shall provide the city a period of forty (40) days prior
to the hearing to consider the request and submit a reply or comment to the
county. If the city submits comment or a letter stating they have no comment
prior to the forty (40) day time period, the period shall commence upon the
date of receipt by the county. After public testimony has been closed for the
final hearing on an application, the city forfeits its right to comment on the
application. Following the receipt by the county of an application or request
for property in the area, a joint application conference may be held with the
applicant and staff from the city and county to review and discuss the
application or request.
      3.   The county shall consider seriously any comment or reply from the
city as part of its hearing process.
   (E)   Inspections: Development or establishment of a land use resulting from
approval of a permit application in the area shall be inspected by the county
when required. The county shall continue to issue all building permits and
mobile home installation permits in the area. The county shall continue to
retain authority over recognizing the approval of all inspections and
certificates of occupancy.
   (F)   Complaints: Complaints that have been received in writing by the
county shall be investigated by the county.
   (G)   Annexation: If an application for a zoning district amendment,
comprehensive plan amendment, or subdivision plat for land located within the
area is received in conjunction with a request for annexation, the application
shall be presented, by the applicant, directly to the city, not the county. The
city shall collect the appropriate fee(s) in accordance with their adopted fee
schedule. In the event the property which is the subject of the application is
annexed by the city while the application is pending before the city, the city
can thereafter make a final determination on the application as though the
property had been within the city at the time the application was made. In the
event that the annexation is not executed prior to the city's final
determination on the application, that decision shall be void. Afterward, the
applicant may wait for the city to annex their property to make a new
application to the city or make application to the county, which will collect
county fees and process the application. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-5: APPEALS:
   (A)   There shall be no appeal of city recommendations offered pursuant to
subsection
10-18A-4(D)2 of this article because such recommendations are not final
determinations. Appeals from county actions shall be governed by the appeal
provisions of the relevant county ordinances, the Idaho Code, the Idaho rules
of civil procedure, and any other applicable statute or regulation.
   (B)   Final decisions by the county made under this agreement may be subject
to appeal or judicial review. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-6: ENFORCEMENT:
The planning and building department and/or the county prosecuting attorney may
take legal action to enforce land use regulations within the area. (Ord. 388,
2-7-2012)
10-18A-7: RENEGOTIATION:
   (A)   This agreement shall be renegotiated at any time upon written request
of either party in accordance with Idaho Code section 67-6526(d).
   (B)   Pursuant to Idaho Code section 67-6526(d), it is the intent of the
parties that the governing boards shall, at least every ten (10) years,
undertake a review of the area of city impact plan and ordinance requirements
to determine whether renegotiations are in the best interests of the citizenry.
(Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
10-18A-8: AGREEMENT WITH LATAH COUNTY:
The mayor of the city of Genesee is hereby authorized to enter into the revised
city of Genesee area of city impact agreement with Latah County which sets
forth and gives effect to the provisions contained herein. (Ord. 388, 2-7-2012)
ARTICLE B. NEZ PERCE COUNTY AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
10-18B-1: Area
10-18B-2: Definitions
10-18B-3: Governing Plan And Ordinances
10-18B-4: Administration Of The Area Of City Impact
10-18B-5: Appeals
10-18B-6: Enforcement
10-18B-7: Renegotiation
10-18B-8: Agreement With Nez Perce County
10-18B-1: AREA:
The Genesee area of city impact agreement shall affect the unincorporated area
of Nez Perce County within the following sections: The North 1/2 of Sections
22, 23, and 24, Township 37 North, Range 5 West, B.M., as depicted on the map
attached to the ordinance codified herein, and as provided in the Genesee area
of city impact agreement and in Nez Perce County ordinance 90. Land outside the
city limits, but within the above described area shall be deemed within the
Genesee area of city impact. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words when used herein shall have these meanings:
   ADMINISTRATIVE REQUESTS: Applications, requests, determinations, or
interpretations other than quasi-judicial and "legislative actions" as defined
herein, such as land divisions, zoning determinations, floodplain
determinations, zoning interpretations of the zoning administrator or designee,
and other administrative actions.
   AREA: The city of Genesee's area of city impact.
   BOARD: The board of Nez Perce County commissioners.
   CITY: The city of Genesee.
   COMPLAINTS: Written requests for enforcement under the ordinances adopted
pursuant to section
10-18B-3 of this article.
   COUNTY: Nez Perce County.
   LEGISLATIVE ACTIONS: Amendments to the zoning map or ordinances, and other
similar decisions by a governing board sitting in a legislative capacity, where
its decision produces a general rule or policy applicable to an open class of
individuals, interests, or situations.
   QUASI-JUDICIAL APPLICATIONS: Applications for decisions or determinations
regarding property located within the area, which are made by a governing board
or its designee sitting in a quasi- judicial capacity, where its decision
involves the application of a general rule or policy to specific individuals,
interests, or situations, including, but not limited to, conditional use
permits, special use permits, planned unit developments, subdivisions,
variances, rezones, and other quasi-judicial proceedings. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-3: GOVERNING PLAN AND ORDINANCES:
   (A)   The county's comprehensive plan (resolution 98-12-153), land use
ordinance (ordinance 72z, as amended), and fee schedule (resolution 2008-11-
178), and subsequent amendments thereto, are hereby adopted by the county for
the area. All other applicable county ordinances and resolutions are still in
effect for the area.
   (B)   The county will adopt or has adopted this agreement in Nez Perce
County ordinance 90. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-4: ADMINISTRATION OF THE AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
   (A)   Administration: The county shall administer the applicable ordinances
and resolutions for the area, as identified in subsection
10-18B-3(A) of this article.
   (B)   Applications, Permits Made To County: All applications, requests for
permits, and inquiries regarding property located within the area, which are
made pursuant to the ordinances adopted under section
10-18B-3 of this article, shall be made to the county. The county shall charge
and collect a fee based upon the adopted county fee schedule, as identified in
subsection
10-18B-3(A) of this article.
   (C)   County To Notify City: The county shall process administrative
requests in the area without input from the city, however, the county will
notify the city of administrative requests, such as building permits or land
divisions, within ten (10) days of receipt of such request. The city and county
recognize that some administrative requests, such as zoning interpretations or
buildable parcel determinations, are informal and can be addressed by county
staff without the need to notify the city.
   (D)   Quasi-Judicial Applications:
      1.   Quasi-judicial applications shall be reviewed by the county staff
and scheduled for the required public hearing(s) before the Nez Perce County
zoning commission and/or the board of county commissioners, as specified by the
Nez Perce County land use ordinance.
      2.   The county shall provide the city a period of forty (40) days prior
to the hearing to consider the request and submit a reply or comment to the
county. If the city submits comment or a letter stating they have no comment
prior to the forty (40) day time period, the period shall commence upon the
date of receipt by the county. After public testimony has been closed for the
final hearing on an application, the city forfeits its right to comment on the
application. Following the receipt by the county of an application or request
for property in the area, a joint application conference may be held with the
applicant and staff from the city and county to review and discuss the
application or request.
      3.   The county shall consider seriously any comment or reply from the
city as part of its hearing process.
   (E)   Inspections: Development or establishment of a land use resulting from
approval of a permit application in the area shall be inspected by the county
when required. The county shall continue to issue all building permits and
mobile home installation permits in the area. The county shall continue to
retain authority over recognizing the approval of all inspections and
certificates of occupancy.
   (F)   Complaints: Complaints that have been received in writing by the
county shall be investigated by the county.
   (G)   Annexation: If an application for a zoning district amendment,
comprehensive plan amendment, or subdivision plat for land located within the
area is received in conjunction with a request for annexation, the application
shall be presented, by the applicant, directly to the city, not the county. The
city shall collect the appropriate fee(s) in accordance with their adopted fee
schedule. In the event the property which is the subject of the application is
annexed by the city while the application is pending before the city, the city
can thereafter make a final determination on the application as though the
property had been within the city at the time the application was made. In the
event that the annexation is not executed prior to the city's final
determination on the application, that decision shall be void. Afterward, the
applicant may wait for the city to annex their property to make a new
application to the city or make application to the county, which will collect
county fees and process the application. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-5: APPEALS:
   (A)   There shall be no appeal of city recommendations offered pursuant to
subsection
10-18B-4(D)2 of this article because such recommendations are not final
determinations. Appeals from county actions shall be governed by the appeal
provisions of the relevant county ordinances, the Idaho Code, the Idaho rules
of civil procedure, and any other applicable statute or regulation.
   (B)   Final decisions by the county made under this agreement may be subject
to appeal or judicial review. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-6: ENFORCEMENT:
The planning and building department and/or the county prosecuting attorney may
take legal action to enforce land use regulations within the area. (Ord. 389,
5-1-2012)
10-18B-7: RENEGOTIATION:
   (A)   This agreement shall be renegotiated at any time upon written request
of either party in accordance with Idaho Code section 67-6526(d).
   (B)   Pursuant to Idaho Code section 67-6526(d), it is the intent of the
parties that the governing boards shall, at least every ten (10) years,
undertake a review of the area of city impact plan and ordinance requirements
to determine whether renegotiations are in the best interests of the citizenry.
(Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
10-18B-8: AGREEMENT WITH NEZ PERCE COUNTY:
The mayor of the city of Genesee is hereby authorized to enter into the city of
Genesee area of city impact agreement with Nez Perce County which sets forth
and gives effect to the provisions contained herein. (Ord. 389, 5-1-2012)
CHAPTER 19
LIVESTOCK AND FOWL 1
SECTION:
10-19-1: Maintaining Certain Animals And Fowl Regulated
10-19-2: Hogs And Pigs
10-19-3: Permission Required To Move Animals
10-19-4: Impounding Fees
10-19-5: Misdemeanor
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 6, chapter 5 of this code.
10-19-1: MAINTAINING CERTAIN ANIMALS AND FOWL REGULATED:
It shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any fowl, rabbits, horses, cows,
sheep, goats or other livestock within the city limits, except as provided in
this section.
   (A)   Zone A shall consist of properties with less than fifteen thousand
(15,000) square feet of real property. Zone B shall consist of properties with
fifteen thousand (15,000) square feet or more but less than fifty thousand
(50,000) square feet of real property. Zone C shall consist of properties of
fifty thousand (50,000) square feet or more of real property.
   (B)   In computing the square footage requirements of this section for
purposes of animals other than rabbits or fowl, the following restrictions
shall apply. In making the zone determination for rabbits and fowl, all real
property which the person owns or controls in accordance with subsection (B)3
of this section may be considered.
      1.   The space occupied by any building and any area excluded from access
by the animals, except buildings to be occupied by the animals, for which the
calculation is being made, shall be excluded.
      2.   The required area for any animal or for animals shall be considered
only one time. For example, the ten thousand (10,000) square feet in zone B
necessary for one horse shall not also be considered in the calculation of the
square footage for one cow.
      3.   The property making up the required area must be owned or leased by
the applicant or the applicant must have the written authorization of the owner
of the property to use the property for the purpose of grazing or maintaining
animals.
      4.   The property which may be considered in making up the square footage
must be adjoining or adjacent which shall be deemed to mean not separated by a
distance greater than the width of a street.
      5.   It shall not be necessary that the animals have continual access to
all of the property, but all property being considered in making up the square
footage shall be devoted primarily to the use of the animals.
   (C)   In zone A, a person may be allowed to keep and maintain one horse or
one cow or two (2) sheep or two (2) goats for every five thousand (5,000)
square feet of real property with a maximum of two (2) horses or two (2) cows
or four (4) sheep or four (4) goats.
   (D)   In zone A, a person may be allowed to keep and maintain up to twenty
five (25) fowl or rabbits, and in no event shall the fowl or poultry hutch or
the fowl, poultry or rabbit run be less than forty feet (40') from any dwelling
other than that of the owner.
   (E)   In zone B, a person may be allowed to keep and maintain one horse or
one cow or four (4) sheep or four (4) goats for every ten thousand (10,000)
square feet of real property with a maximum of five (5) horses or five (5) cows
or ten (10) sheep or ten (10) goats. In zone C, a person may be allowed to keep
and maintain one horse or one cow or four (4) sheep or four (4) goats for every
ten thousand (10,000) square feet of real property with a maximum of ten (10)
horses and ten (10) cows or twenty (20) sheep or twenty (20) goats.
   (F)   In zones B and C, a person shall be allowed to keep and maintain up to
fifty (50) fowl or rabbits, and in no event shall the fowl or poultry house,
rabbit hutch or the fowl, poultry or rabbit run be less than forty feet (40')
from any dwelling other than that of the owner.
   (G)   It shall be lawful to maintain or keep offspring of any cow, horse,
goat or sheep, in addition to the animals herein allowed, for a period of six
(6) months after the birth of such offspring and, and it shall be lawful to
maintain and keep the offspring of any rabbit or fowl in addition to the rabbit
or fowl herein allowed for a period of twelve (12) weeks.
   (H)   In the event the city shall receive two (2) written complaints
regarding the keeping or maintaining of animals, including, but not limited to,
the property classification of properties, from residents of the city within
any three (3) month period, the complaints shall be referred to the commission
for consideration. The party complained against may be directed to make
application for approval of his keeping and maintaining animals, which
application shall be made and processed in the same manner as a special review
use application as set out in section
10-8-6 of this title. The approving agency shall have all authority and powers
regarding modifications and conditions as set out in section
10-8-6 of this title notwithstanding any provision of this chapter, including
authority to reduce the animals or fowl which may be allowed to something less
than is otherwise allowed hereby even to the extent of allowing no animals
whatsoever to be kept or maintained on the property under consideration. The
result of such proceedings shall be the approval of such party keeping and
maintaining animals as he was doing prior to the receipt of two (2) written
complaints or the imposition of appropriate restrictions on his keeping and
maintaining animals. Any party subjected to a restriction hereunder may present
an application in accordance with section
10-8-6 of this title to remove such restriction not less than two (2) years
after the effective date of such restriction. Any restrictions imposed are
personal to the party against whom such restrictions are imposed and do not
apply to subsequent occupiers of the same property. In the event a party fails
to make applications for approval within fifteen (15) days after being directed
to do so, then the commission may proceed to publish notice of a public hearing
based on the complaints received in accordance with subsection
10-8-6(B)3 of this title and may thereafter impose such restrictions as the
commission deems appropriate. The action taken by the approving agency shall
not affect the criminal prosecution of violations of this chapter in any way.
(Ord. 290, 2-2-1987)
10-19-2: HOGS AND PIGS:
It shall be unlawful to maintain any hogs or pigs within zone A. Hogs and pigs
may be allowed in zones B and C for the period of April to October in the same
numbers as horses may be allowed in zones B and C with the same provision for
offspring as stated herein. There must be at least fifty (50) square feet of
enclosed real property for each hog or pig more than six (6) months old. In no
event shall the space containing hogs or pigs be less than forty feet (40')
from a dwelling other than that of the owner. (Ord. 290, 2-2-1987)
10-19-3: PERMISSION REQUIRED TO MOVE ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive or cause to be driven any loose
animals or fowl whatsoever in, on, through or across any street or alley within
the municipality without first having obtained the consent of the chief of
police. Provided, however, that any person may drive not to exceed one head of
any such loose animal or fowl through or across any street or alley without
first having obtained consent of the said chief of police. In the event animals
or fowl shall have escaped from their enclosure, it shall not be necessary to
obtain permission to return the animals to an enclosure. (Ord. 290, 2-2-1987)
10-19-4: IMPOUNDING FEES:
The chief of police shall be entitled to receive for the municipality as legal
fees for taking up and impounding horses, mules, cattle, hogs, sheep and goats
or other livestock, twenty five dollars ($25.00) per head; for chickens or
other fowl or rabbits, two dollars fifty cents ($2.50) each. For keeping
animals, his charges per day shall be as follows: horses, mules, cattle, hogs,
sheep and goats, five dollars ($5.00); rabbits, chickens or other fowl, two
dollars ($2.00). (Ord. 290, 2-2-1987)
10-19-5: MISDEMEANOR:
   (A)   It is hereby declared a misdemeanor to maintain or keep animals or
fowl in violation of the requirements of this chapter.
   (B)   It is hereby declared a misdemeanor to allow dead fowl, rabbit, calf,
sheep, or goat bodies, other than those slaughtered for consumption, to remain
upon the ground or in stables or in the particular animal run longer than
twenty four (24) hours. It is hereby declared a misdemeanor to allow dead cow,
horse or hog bodies, other than those slaughtered for consumption, to remain
upon the ground or in stables or in the particular animal run longer than three
(3) days. (Ord. 290, 2-2-1987)
CHAPTER 20
MANUFACTURED HOUSING
SECTION:
10-20-1: Definitions
10-20-2: Requirements For Manufactured Homes On Individual Lots
10-20-3: Class A Manufactured Homes On Individual Lots
10-20-4: Class B Manufactured Homes On Individual Building Lots
10-20-5: Replacement Of Nonconforming Manufactured Homes
10-20-6: Repeal Of Inconsistent Provisions
10-20-7: Provisions Severable
10-20-8: Effective Date
10-20-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions are provided for the purpose of proper interpretation
and administration of this chapter:
   CLASS A MANUFACTURED HOME: A manufactured home meeting the following
standards:
   (A)   Constructed after January 1, 1985, and certified as meeting current
mobile home construction and safety standards of the department of housing and
urban development.
   (B)   At least twenty feet (20') wide at the narrowest point.
   (C)   Roof pitch shall be not less than two foot (2') rise for each twelve
feet (12') of horizontal run (2:12) and roof shall have minimum six inch (6")
eave or eave and gutter.
   (D)   Has roofing materials which are in general use for site built housing;
however, any roofing material may be used provided it has the appearance of a
nonmetallic shingle, shake or tile roof.
   (E)   Has siding material which has the appearance of wood, masonry or
horizontal metal siding. Reflection from horizontal metal siding shall be no
greater than that from siding coated with white gloss enamel.
   (F)   Has a perimeter foundation constructed of brick, concrete, concrete
block or pressure treated wood, or is fully skirted with material having the
same appearance.
   (G)   Hitch or tongue of manufactured home shall be removed.
   CLASS B MANUFACTURED HOME: A manufactured home meeting the mobile home
construction and safety standards of the department of housing and urban
development but not meeting all of criteria (A) through (G) of class A
manufactured homes defined herein.
   CLASS C MANUFACTURED HOME: A manufactured home which does not meet the
mobile home construction and safety standards of the department of housing and
urban development but which is at least ten feet (10') wide and forty feet
(40') in length. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
10-20-2: REQUIREMENTS FOR MANUFACTURED HOMES ON INDIVIDUAL LOTS:
   (A)   Manufactured homes on individual lots shall conform to all setback,
placement, lot size, and other requirements of this title for conventionally
built single-family homes on individual lots.
   (B)   Manufactured homes shall be connected to and served by the same
utility systems as provide service to conventionally built residences and shall
contain heating, plumbing, illumination, cooking and electrical equipment and
installations which conform to the standards adopted by the city for
conventionally built residences within the city.
   (C)   Only one manufactured home may be placed on an individual lot.
   (D)   Manufactured homes shall comply to chapter 13 of this title relating
to the location of mobile homes in floodplain areas and any other applicable
requirements of this section.
   (E)   The following requirements shall apply to any accessory structure to a
manufactured home on an individual lot:
      1.   An accessory building or structure, as is permitted in the zoning
district in which the manufactured home is to be located, shall be similar to
material and integrated into the design of the primary structure.
      2.   Accessory buildings or structures shall meet the uniform building
code standards or United States department of housing and urban development
standards. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
10-20-3: CLASS A MANUFACTURED HOMES ON INDIVIDUAL LOTS:
Class A manufactured homes are allowed on individual building lots, providing
that a permit for placement is secured at least seven (7) days prior to
placement. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
10-20-4: CLASS B MANUFACTURED HOMES ON INDIVIDUAL BUILDING LOTS:
   (A)   A class B manufactured home shall be allowed on any individual
building lot within the city of Genesee only under the following circumstances:
      1.   The mobile home has been inspected and approved by the United States
department of housing and urban development (HUD) and bears the seal of that
department, and
      2.   A conditional use permit has been obtained from the planning and
zoning commission of the city of Genesee, Idaho, based on a finding that
approval of the applicant for a conditional use permit will be compatible with
the general character of the neighborhood and will not negatively affect values
of other property within the neighborhood.
   (B)   In making its determination, the commission shall consider at least
the following criteria:
      1.   Existence of other similar manufactured homes in the neighborhood.
      2.   The general character of the neighborhood including the existing
land uses, compatibility of types and styles of buildings and condition of
housing.
   (C)   Approval of conditional use permit shall require that the applicant
comply with the following requirements:
      1.   The manufactured home shall be permanently attached to the real
property of the lot upon which the manufactured home is situated by anchoring
the manufactured home to a concrete foundation, removing the tongue and wheels
from the manufactured home and installing skirting acceptable to the commission
around the entire circumference of the manufactured home.
      2.   A building permit for the placement of the manufactured home on the
foundation on the lot shall be obtained from the building department of the
city of Genesee at least seven (7) days prior to placement.
      3.   A certificate of occupancy for the manufactured home shall be
obtained from the building department of the city of Genesee. (Ord. 324, 5-16-
1994)
10-20-5: REPLACEMENT OF NONCONFORMING MANUFACTURED HOMES:
   (A)   Replacement Of Nonconforming Homes: Nonconforming manufactured homes
located on individual lots which are removed from the property shall be
replaced only by conforming units.
   (B)   Destruction Of A Nonconforming Use: If a nonconforming manufactured
home is destroyed by any cause to an extent exceeding fifty percent (50%) of
fair market value as indicated by the records of the county assessor, a future
structure or use on the site shall conform to this chapter. (Ord. 324, 5-16-
1994)
10-20-6: REPEAL OF INCONSISTENT PROVISIONS:
Any provision of this code which is inconsistent with a provision of this title
is hereby repealed to the extent of such inconsistency. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
10-20-7: PROVISIONS SEVERABLE:
The provisions of this chapter shall be deemed severable and as finding that
any provision is unlawful or unconstitutional by a court having jurisdiction
shall not affect the remaining provisions. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
10-20-8: EFFECTIVE DATE:
This chapter shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage,
approval and publication according to law. (Ord. 324, 5-16-1994)
CHAPTER 21
SMALL WIND ENERGY SYSTEMS
SECTION:
10-21-1: Definitions
10-21-2: Location
10-21-3: Visual Appearance, Lighting, And Power Lines
10-21-4: Tower Type
10-21-5: Sound Levels And Measurement
10-21-6: Minimum Ground Clearance
10-21-7: Safety
10-21-8: Compliance With Building Codes
10-21-9: Compliance With Electrical Code
10-21-10: Compliance With Federal Aviation Administration Regulations
10-21-11: Other Federal, State And Local Requirements
10-21-12: Removal Of Defective Or Abandoned Small Wind Energy Systems
10-21-1: DEFINITIONS:
   SMALL WIND ENERGY SYSTEM: A wind energy conversion system consisting of wind
turbine(s), tower(s), and associated control or conversion electronics, which
has a rated capacity of not more than one hundred (100) kilowatts, turbine
height no greater than one hundred twenty five feet (125') and which is
intended to primarily reduce on site consumption of utility power.
   TURBINE HEIGHT: The distance measured from grade level of the tower
foundation to the highest point of the turbine rotor plane. (Ord. 382, 11-18-
2010)
10-21-2: LOCATION:
   (A)   Small wind energy systems and all towers, flagpoles and other similar
vertical structures shall be a permitted use in all zoning classifications in
the city of Genesee subject to the following requirements:
      1.   Must be located on a lot that has a minimum of seven thousand five
hundred (7,500) square feet of unobstructed property.
      2.   Must be situated so that its height is not greater than a distance
one and one-half (11/2) times the distance to the nearest lot boundary.
      3.   Total height must not exceed sixty feet (60') above the highest
elevation on the lot.
      4.   No aboveground part or component of a small wind energy system,
including, but not limited to, guywire anchors, may extend closer than one and
one-half (11/2) times the turbine height to the nearest boundary of the lot
upon which it is located.
      5.   A small wind energy system shall be set back from the nearest
aboveground public or private nonparticipating electric power line or telephone
line a distance of no less than one and two- tenths (1.2) times the turbine
height, determined from the existing power line or telephone line. (Ord. 382,
11-18-2010)
10-21-3: VISUAL APPEARANCE, LIGHTING, AND POWER LINES:
   (A)   The wind turbines of a small wind energy system shall be painted a
nonreflective, nonobtrusive color. Small wind energy system towers shall
maintain galvanized steel, brushed aluminum, white or gray finish, unless
federal aviation administration standards require otherwise.
   (B)   No small wind energy system shall be artificially lighted, except to
the extent required by the federal aviation administration or other applicable
authority.
   (C)   No small wind energy system shall be used for displaying any
advertising except for reasonable identification of the manufacturer.
   (D)   Electrical controls, control wiring and power lines shall be wireless
or underground after reaching grade from the turbine and extending away from
the base of the tower. Wiring may be exposed vertically from the turbine to the
base of the tower. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-4: TOWER TYPE:
   (A)   Guyed, lattice and monopole towers are allowed to support the wind
turbines of a small wind energy system, and must meet current engineering
standards pertaining to durability and safety. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-5: SOUND LEVELS AND MEASUREMENT:
   (A)   During construction and operations, a small wind energy system shall
comply with applicable state and county noise standards and the city of Genesee
nuisance ordinance. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-6: MINIMUM GROUND CLEARANCE:
   (A)   The rotor blade tip of any small wind energy system shall, at its
lowest point, have ground clearance of no less than fifteen feet (15') as
measured at the lowest point of the arc of the rotor blade. (Ord. 382, 11-18-
2010)
10-21-7: SAFETY:
   (A)   Monopole towers shall not be climbable up to fifteen feet (15') above
ground level. A lattice type tower shall have a fence around it that is a
minimum of six feet (6') in height.
   (B)   All electrical equipment shall be safely and appropriately enclosed
from unintentional access by means such as barrier fencing, equipment cabinetry
or similar means. All access doors to electrical equipment shall remain locked
when not attended.
   (C)   Appropriate warning signage regarding, but not limited to, electrical
hazards, shall be placed on all small wind energy systems and surrounding fence
(if fence is required).
   (D)   All small wind energy systems shall be equipped with manual and
automatic overspeed controls to limit rotation of the rotor blades to a speed
below the designed limits of the system. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-8: COMPLIANCE WITH BUILDING CODES:
   (A)   Small wind energy systems shall comply with the Idaho state building
code and adopted international building code.
   (B)   All construction of a tower, flagpole, and other similar vertical
structure requires a current building permit from the city of Genesee.
   (C)   Application for a building permit to the city of Genesee for the
construction of a small wind energy system shall include standard drawings and
an engineering analysis of the system's tower, showing compliance with current
city of Genesee building code and international building code. The engineering
must include a complete analysis of the tower, the tower foundation and the
connection of the tower to the foundation. The engineering analysis must be
completed by a licensed engineer, certified to practice in the state of Idaho.
(Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-9: COMPLIANCE WITH ELECTRICAL CODE:
   (A)   Small wind energy systems shall comply with requirements of the Idaho
Code, applicable state of Idaho regulations, city of Genesee, and the current
adopted edition of the national electric code (NEC). (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-10: COMPLIANCE WITH FEDERAL AVIATION ADMINISTRATION REGULATIONS:
   (A)   Small wind energy systems must comply with all regulations of the
federal aviation administration, including any necessary approvals for
installations close to airports. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-11: OTHER FEDERAL, STATE AND LOCAL REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Small wind energy systems shall comply with all applicable federal,
state and county laws, codes and policies.
   (B)   Small wind energy systems that are connected to the utility grid shall
comply with the requirements of Idaho Code and applicable state of Idaho
regulations. (Ord. 382, 11-18-2010)
10-21-12: REMOVAL OF DEFECTIVE OR ABANDONED SMALL WIND ENERGY SYSTEMS:
   (A)   Any small wind energy system found to be unsafe by the city of Genesee
building official shall not be operated and shall be promptly repaired by the
landowner, at the landowner's expense, to meet federal, state and local safety
standards and regulations, or shall be removed within three (3) months.
   (B)   If any small wind energy system is not operational for a period of
twelve (12) consecutive months or more, the city of Genesee may request by
registered mail that the landowner provide corrective action. The landowner
will have forty five (45) days to respond setting forth specific reasons for
the operational difficulty and provide a reasonable timetable for corrective
action. If the city of Genesee deems the timetable for corrective action is
unreasonable, it shall notify the landowner and such landowner shall remove the
small wind energy system at his or her own expense within one hundred twenty
(120) days of receipt of notice from the city of Genesee. The city of Genesee
shall have the authority to pursue legal action if necessary. (Ord. 382, 11-18-
2010)

10-22-1: STATUTORY AUTHORIZATION, FINDINGS OF FACT, PURPOSE, AND OBJECTIVES:
10-22-1-1: STATUTORY AUTHORITY:
The Legislature of the State of Idaho, pursuant to Idaho Code §§ 46-1020, 46-
1023, and 46-1024, authorizes local governments to adopt floodplain management
ordinances that identify floodplains and minimum floodplain development
standards to minimize flood hazards and protect human life, health, and
property. Therefore, the Council of the City of Genesee, Idaho does hereby
ordain as follows. (Ord. 428, 11-1-2022)
10-22-1-2: FINDINGS OF FACT:
   (A)   The flood hazard areas of City of Genesee are subject to periodic
inundation that results in:
      1.   Loss of life and property;
      2.   Health and safety hazards;
      3.   Disruption of commerce and governmental services;
      4.   Extraordinary public expenditures for flood relief and protection;
and
      5.   Impairment of the tax base, all of which adversely affect the public
health, safety, and general welfare.
   (B)   These flood losses may be caused by development in flood hazard areas,
which are inadequately elevated, flood-proofed, or otherwise unprotected from
flood damages, and by the cumulative effect of obstructions in floodplains
causing increases in flood heights and velocities.
   (C)   Local government units have the primary responsibility for planning,
adopting, and enforcing land use regulations to accomplish proper floodplain
management. (Ord. 428, 11-1-2022)
10-22-1-3: STATEMENT OF PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to promote public health, safety, and general
welfare and to minimize public and private losses due to flood conditions in
specific areas by provisions designed to:
   (A)   Protect human life, health, and property;
   (B)   Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water
purification and sewage treatment plants, water and gas mains, electric,
telephone and sewer lines, streets, and bridges located in floodplains;
   (C)   Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and
development of flood prone areas;
   (D)   Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control
projects;
   (E)   Minimize the need for rescue and emergency services associated with
flooding, generally undertaken at the expense of the general public;
   (F)   Minimize prolonged business interruptions;
   (G)   Ensure potential buyers are notified the property is in an area of
special flood hazard; and
   (H)   Ensure those who occupy the areas of special flood hazard assume
responsibility for their actions. (Ord. 428, 11-1-2022)
10-22-1-4: OBJECTIVES AND METHODS OF REDUCING FLOOD LOSSES:
In order to accomplish its purpose, this chapter includes methods and
provisions to:
   (A)   Require that development which is vulnerable to floods, including
structures and facilities necessary for the general health, safety, and welfare
of citizens, be protected against flood damage at the time of initial
construction;
   (B)   Restrict or prohibit development which are dangerous to health,
safety, and property due to water or erosion hazards, or which increase flood
heights, velocities, or erosion;
   (C)   Control filling, grading, dredging, and other development which may
increase flood damage or erosion;
   (D)   Prevent or regulate the construction of flood barriers that will
unnaturally divert flood waters or that may increase flood hazards to other
lands;
   (E)   Preserve and restore natural floodplains, stream channels, and natural
protective barriers which carry and store flood waters. (Ord. 428, 11-1-2022)

               A general term used to refer to the several types of revisions and amendments to
               FIRMs that can be accomplished by letter. They include Letter of Map Amendment
               (LOMA), Letter of Map Revision (LOMR), and Letter of Map Revision based on Fill
               (LOMR-F):
               (A)   Letter of Map Amendment (LOMA): an official amendment, by letter, to an
               effective National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP) map. A LOMA establishes a
               property's or structure's location in relation to the Special Flood Hazard Area
               (SFHA). LOMAs are usually issued because a property or structure has been
               inadvertently mapped as being in the floodplain but is actually on natural high
               ground above the base flood elevation.
               (B)   Letter of Map Revision (LOMR): FEMA's modification to an effective Flood
               Insurance Rate Map (FIRM) or a Flood Boundary and Floodway Map (FBFM) or both. LOMRs
               are generally based on the implementation of physical measures that affect the
               hydrologic or hydraulic characteristics of a flooding source and thus result in the
               modification of the existing regulatory floodway, the effective Base Flood
LETTER OF MAP  Elevations (BFEs), or the Special Flood Hazard Area (SFHA). The LOMR officially
CHANGE (LOMC): revises the Flood Insurance Rate Map (FIRM) or Flood Boundary and Floodway Map
               (FBFM), and sometimes the Flood Insurance Study (FIS) report, and when appropriate,
               includes a description of the modifications. The LOMR is generally accompanied by an
               annotated copy of the affected portions of the FIRM, FBFM, or FIS report.
               (C)   Letter of Map Revision Based on Fill (LOMR-F): FEMA's modification of the
               Special Flood Hazard Area (SFHA) shown on the Flood Insurance Rate Map (FIRM) based
               on the placement of fill outside the existing regulatory floodway. The LOMR-F does
               not change the FIRM, FBFM, or FIS report.
               (D)   Conditional Letter of Map Revision (CLOMR): A formal review and comment as to
               whether a proposed flood protection project or other project complies with the
               minimum NFIP requirements for such projects with respect to delineation of special
               flood hazard areas. A CLOMR does not revise the effective Flood Insurance Rate Map
               (FIRM) or Flood Insurance Study (FIS). Upon submission and approval of certified as-
               built documentation, a Letter of Map Revision (LOMR) may be issued by FEMA to revise
               the effective FIRM. Building Permits and/or Flood Development Permits cannot be
               issued based on a CLOMR, because a CLOMR does not change the NFIP map.
               A man-made structure, usually an earthen embankment, designed and constructed
LEVEE:         according to sound engineering practices, to contain, control, or divert the flow of
               water so as to provide protection from temporary flooding.
               A flood protection system that consists of a levee, or levees, and associated
LEVEE SYSTEM:  structures, such as closure and drainage devices, which are constructed and operated
               in accordance with sound engineering practices.
LOWEST         The lowest point of the ground level next to the structure. Refer to the FEMA

(LAG):
               The lowest floor of the lowest enclosed area (including basement). An unfinished or

               The act of ongoing upkeep of existing structures required to keep channels in a

               A structure, transportable in one or more sections, built on a permanent chassis and
MANUFACTURED   designed to be used with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the
HOME:          required utilities. This includes tiny homes and park model manufactured homes. The
               term "Manufactured Home" does not include a "Recreational Vehicle."

HOME PARK OR   lots for rent or sale.
SUBDIVISION:
               The building value, not including the land value and that of any accessory
MARKET VALUE:  structures or other improvements on the lot. Market value may be established by

               For purposes of the National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP), the National Geodetic
MEAN SEA       Vertical Datum (NGVD) of 1929 or other datum (such as North America Vertical Datum
LEVEL:         of 1988 - NAVD88) to which Base Flood Elevations (BFEs) shown on a community's FIRM
               are referenced.
               Describes a condition where there is a river, flow, or inundation of liquid mud down
               a hillside usually as a result of a dual condition of loss of brush cover and the
MUDSLIDE       subsequent accumulation of water on the ground preceded by a period of unusually
(I.E.,         heavy or sustained rain. A mudslide (i.e., mudflow) may occur as a distinct
MUDFLOW):      phenomenon while a landslide is in progress, and will be recognized as such by the
               Administrator only if the mudflow, and not the landslide, is the proximate cause of
               damage that occurs.
MUDSLIDE       The operation of an overall program of corrective and preventive measures for

MUDFLOW) AREA  preparedness plans, mudslide control works, and flood plain management regulations.
